**Update protocol:** When a bundle locks design for an interpretation surface, the surface contract is added to this file and the file version increments. Master Reference + handoff doc reference this file's current version. **V8 LOCKED → V9 OPEN convention:** V7 + V8 are now both LOCKED — no further in-place amendments allowed; V7-only and V8-only references in this document remain as historical record. V9 is OPEN with the same in-place amendment convention V7/V8 used: bundles that ship between V9-open and V9-lock amend V9 in place rather than incrementing to V10. V9 LOCKS when at least one of the three tracked amendments (V9.1 / V9.2 / V9.3) lands, or auto-locks empty if no triggers fire within reasonable post-launch timeframe.
**Connection to verification:** B10b (narrative coherence verification, planned post-B9) consumes this file as the source of truth. Each contract block defines its own three layers of test (boundary fidelity, non-redundancy, cumulative narrative).

---

## 1. Purpose

The product ships ~9 interpretation surfaces that each interpret the underlying evaluation data for the user. As surfaces accumulate across V4S28 bundles (B1 → B4 → B5 → B6 → B7 → B8 → B9), the cross-surface overlap risk compounds: each surface is locked individually against its audit finding, but no system-level check verifies that the surfaces collectively *tell different stories*.

The risk this document protects against: a user reading the full evaluation feels the system repeats itself. Risk 3 says "founder needs hospital CFO relationships." Main Bottleneck says "Trust/credibility — hospital CFO trust gates everything." Evidence Strength says "uncertainty around hospital CFO buyer behavior." Three sections, three labels, one underlying narrative — that's overlap, not depth.

This document records what each surface MUST own and MUST NOT drift into. Future verification (B10b) treats these contracts as ground truth: any surface drifting into another's territory is a contract violation, regardless of whether the prose looks fine in isolation.

## 2. The unique-question principle

The principle, applied to every interpretation surface in the product:

> Each surface owns exactly one user question. If two surfaces answer the same question with different words, one surface fails its purpose. If a surface answers a question that no other surface owns, it earns its place.

This is Step 0 of the Five Methodology Principles ("What unique user question does this section answer that no other section answers?") applied **prospectively** to surface design rather than retroactively to fixes. Each contract below states:

- The unique question the surface owns
- Adjacent surfaces and what would constitute drift into their territory
- Anchor predicates (words/phrases that legitimately appear in this surface and only this one)
- Forbidden predicates (words/phrases that should never appear because they belong to another)
- Cross-references allowed (when this surface may legitimately reference another's content)

**Scoring composite (V4S28 B8, May 1, 2026):** Overall = MD × 0.375 + MO × 0.3125 + OR × 0.3125. TC removed from Overall composite — TC is framed UI-side as "execution context · build difficulty," remains a first-class metric with its own rubric and isolated Stage TC scoring call, but does NOT contribute to the Overall number. Score tier labels (V31-style "Strong Opportunity / Viable but Competitive / etc.") KILLED in V4S26b — Score Guide popup is the user-facing interpretation surface for the Overall number. Pre-B8 historical formula preserved for context: `Overall = MD × 0.30 + MO × 0.25 + OR × 0.25 + (10 - TC) × 0.20`. Reasoning for the change: TC measures something different in kind (build difficulty against the founder's profile) from MD/MO/OR (idea quality against the market); bundling them produced silent score compression (most ideas score TC 6-8 → constant 1.2-1.6 point drag on Overall) without adding explanatory power.

## 3. Locked contracts (organized by bundle)

> **[V11.14 / V73 coherence note (June 10 2026):** every locked surface below is a **Deep-mode** contract. Deep = the V5.0 chained engine; in the body and the V9.x records, **"Pro pipeline" = Deep** and **"Free pipeline" = the legacy single-call light path (`prompt.js`) that Explore supersedes**. The Free/Pro TIER language is retired → PAYG + two modes; the engine PATHS and these contracts are UNCHANGED, so read them as-is through that mapping. **Explore** (the expand mode) is a NEW engine whose surfaces (The Read / Angles / The Open Lane / Next Move) are DESIGNED-NOT-BUILT and enter here via the §5 Update Protocol when built. Header-locked guardrail: Explore uses ONE coarse readiness signal per branch, NEVER a multi-axis rubric — a rubric would rebuild these Deep scoring surfaces inside Explore. The Execution Brief is Deep-only.]**

### 3.1 — TC Explanation (technical_complexity output)

**Bundle:** Pre-V4S28 origin (V4S10–V4S11 isolation work). B2 was scoped as no-work / protect-from-spillover — TC explanation behavior was sound at audit time, no V4S28 modifications shipped.
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage-tc.js` → `technical_complexity` JSON output → frontend metric card.
**Locked design source:** `prompt-stage-tc.js` (production); audit-findings.md Section 5 (lines 659–796).

**MUST own:** *"How hard is this product to build for THIS specific user, and where should they start to de-risk?"*

The surface answers the build-difficulty question through three structured fields:
- `base_score_explanation` — the hardest engineering challenge in the product, anchored to a calibration anchor example.
- `adjustment_explanation` — why the founder's professional background adjusts the base score up or down.
- `explanation` — final positioning of the score relative to the named anchor product.
- `incremental_note` — optional simpler starting point for de-risking the build.

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Market territory** (MD's job): never claims about market size, buyer urgency, demand signals, or whether the market is well-understood. TC evaluates idea against founder, not against market.
- **Monetization territory** (MO's job): never claims about pricing, willingness-to-pay, or buyer economics.
- **Originality territory** (OR's job): never claims about competitive replication, defensibility, or differentiation.
- **Founder-fit non-technical territory** (Risk 3 founder_fit slot's job): never references distribution access, network gaps, domain credibility, capital runway, or sales motion as TC factors. TC measures *technical build difficulty*; non-technical execution gaps belong to Risk 3.
- **Binding constraint territory** (Main Bottleneck's job): never identifies the *single binding constraint* that gates the idea. TC may be high without being the binding constraint.
- **Evidence quality territory** (Evidence Strength's job): never comments on how grounded the evaluation is.

**Anchor predicates** (legitimately TC's, should not appear elsewhere):

- Anchor citations: "matches the [X] anchor at [Y]"
- Engineering challenges named concretely: "HIPAA infrastructure", "real-time safety-critical systems", "fine-tuning workflows", "custom retrieval", "audit trail systems"
- Technical adjustment language: "domain-relevant background reduces by 0.5", "adjacent technical experience reduces by 1.0"
- Beyond-tutorial gap markers: "requires specialized engineering knowledge", "cannot be built from documentation alone"
- Incremental starting points: "could start with [simpler version]"

**Forbidden predicates** (these belong to other surfaces):

- "Buyer access" / "distribution" / "network" / "relationships" → these are Risk 3 + Main Bottleneck territory
- "Market is crowded" / "well-understood market" / "buyer urgency" → MD territory
- "Pricing" / "willingness to pay" / "monetization gap" → MO territory
- "Defensibility" / "moat" / "incumbent replication" → OR territory
- "Founder lacks credibility" / "founder lacks domain access" → Risk 3 territory (TC may say "founder lacks technical experience" — that's a build-difficulty claim, not a credibility claim)
- "Binding constraint" / "the bottleneck" → Main Bottleneck territory

**Cross-references allowed:**

- May reference profile facts that affect technical adjustment ("paralegal background"), but only as build-difficulty input, not as domain-credibility commentary.
- May reference the anchor product comparison ("matches the B2B SaaS with integrations anchor"), since the anchor list is internal to TC.
- Should NOT reference Stage 1 output, Stage 2a packets, or competition data — TC runs in isolation by design (V4S11 quarantine work).

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- TC explanation must contain at least one anchor citation match (regex: `matches the [a-z\s,/]+anchor`).
- TC explanation must NOT contain any forbidden predicate from the list above.
- For the same idea + 3 profiles (e.g., MAT1 matrix), `base_score_explanation` should be near-identical (idea-driven), `adjustment_explanation` should differ (profile-driven), `explanation` should differ accordingly. This is the "TC isolation working" shape.
- TC explanation length budget: 3–4 sentences total across all three fields. No section bloat.

**B6-surfaced observation (April 28, 2026 — TC adjustment-math anchor-fixing):**

B6 verification exposed a TC scoring bug not present in the original audit. On the MAT1 trio test (same legal document automation idea × Beginner / Intermediate / Senior profiles), all three profiles produced final TC = 7.0 despite stated adjustments of 0.0 / -0.5 / -1.0 respectively. Per the locked rubric these should have produced 7.0 / 6.5 / 5.5–6.0. Two failure modes visible in the data:

1. **Stated adjustment not applied to score** (MAT1-Intermediate): explanation says "reducing complexity by 0.5 points" but final score equals the unadjusted base (7.0).
2. **Silent base inflation** (MAT1-Senior): explanation cites the same "7.0 multiple API integrations" anchor as the other two profiles BUT the adjustment_explanation states "reducing complexity by 1.0 point from base 8.0" — the base was retroactively inflated to 8.0 in the explanation so the math reconciles to the final 7.0 score.

Both patterns are **anchor-fixing**: the model decides the final score independently and reverse-engineers base + adjustment to match. The contract's "TC isolation working" shape (base near-identical, adjustment differing, explanation differing accordingly) was assumed to be the only failure mode this verification needed to catch. It is not. A second failure mode — stated adjustment values that don't propagate to the score — was missed because the verification looked at score variance rather than internal arithmetic consistency.

**Status:** Discovered in B6. **Deferred to pre-B10a TC scoring discipline session** (B2 reopened from no-work to single-session-pre-B10a).

**Monitoring directive for sessions B7 through B9:** any TC misbehavior surfaced during downstream bundle verification (e.g., MAT-trio TC scores inconsistent with stated adjustments, anchor citations conflicting with adjustment math, profile-aware adjustments producing 0-spread scores) is logged under B2 in execution-plan.md (not patched in-bundle). The pre-B10a session opens with the accumulated observations and lands a structural fix — likely an enforcement step requiring `score = base_score + adjustment_value` arithmetic consistency, with the model surfacing both numeric values explicitly so the relationship is verifiable.

**Why deferred not fixed in B6:** the bug is independent of every B6 surface (Stage 1 prompt + profile strips do not touch TC). Fixing in B6 would require touching `prompt-stage-tc.js`, violating the V4S28 protection directive (Section 5: "do not modify `prompt-stage-tc.js` during V4S28"). Pre-B10a is the natural surfacing point — by then, B7/B8/B9 verification will have surfaced enough TC observations to choose the structural fix correctly rather than guessing at which symptom matters most.

---

#### §3.1 V9.20 amendment (May 17, 2026 — Stage TC structural session + calibration patch; V9.1 LANDED)

**V9.1 amendment STATUS: LANDED.** Carried since V7 LOCK May 4, 2026 as conditional pre-V4S29 amendment triggered on B10a TC gate failure or post-V4S28 polish. Empirical re-analysis of B10a corpus during V4S29 Stage TC session confirmed deterministic ~80-85% arithmetic mismatch across 155 Pro runs (May 5 + May 10 datasets combined), 100% within-rerun stability (Bundle 2 sampler hardening stabilized values but NOT arithmetic consistency), 100% one-directional inflation (scores > math-expected, never lower). MAT1 trio passing canonical gate {7.5, 7.0, 6.0} ± 0.5 with spread ≥1.0 monotonic but anchor-fixed underneath — the gate measured final values not prose-vs-score arithmetic consistency, so the bug went undetected. B9 closure analysis (May 4, 2026) which concluded "sampling artifact, n=1 per profile, NOT a real bug" was wrong; N=155 deterministic disproves the sampling-artifact hypothesis. V9.1 now formally resolves via V9.20 structural rewrite.

**V9.20 structural rewrite (full prompt replacement):**

`prompt-stage-tc.js` fully replaced (316 lines structural rewrite + 34 lines calibration patch = 350 lines total) as drop-in replacement preserving `STAGE_TC_SYSTEM_PROMPT` export. **5-layer arithmetic enforcement architecture:**

1. **Ontology block** (Row 3) — states TC as relational measurement: `score = base_score + adjustment_value` is contract, not optional reasoning step.
2. **Pre-scoring chain Q4 math step** — procedural anti-anchor-fixing: (a) choose base_score from calibration anchor → (b) choose adjustment_value from founder profile → (c) compute score = base + adjustment, with 1.0 floor clamp.
3. **Anti-anchor-fixing CRITICAL block** (Row 9) — behavioral: "Do not decide the final score first and then write base_score or adjustment_value to justify it. The final score is derived, not chosen. If the computed score feels wrong, reconsider the anchor match or the adjustment rung, then recompute. Do not adjust base_score, adjustment_value, or their explanations after seeing the score to make them match."
4. **Scoring rule 4** (Row 18) — `score MUST equal base_score + adjustment_value. Numeric values and prose claims must reconcile.`
5. **JSON schema** (Row 19) — 6-field shape with explicit numeric `base_score` and `adjustment_value` fields enforcing the relationship at output validation layer.

**Adjustment ladder** (V9.20 NEW) — `adjustment_value` constrained to discrete enum `{0, -0.5, -1.0, -1.5}` replacing old "reduce 0.5-1.5 points" range language. Semantic ladder:
- `0`: profile does not materially reduce this build difficulty.
- `-0.5`: limited/domain/contextual help; founder understands the space but does not bring directly applicable build experience. Also applies when general software engineering ability gives broad capability but no specific layer match for this product. (Calibration patch extended this rung to explicitly absorb "general engineering" cases that were drifting to -1.0.)
- `-1.0`: strong adjacent technical or operational help. The founder has worked near the SPECIFIC technical layer or workflow this product depends on. General software engineering ability is not enough for -1.0; if the founder is generally capable but has not worked near this product's specific layer, use -0.5. (Calibration patch tightened from "near the technical or workflow layer this product touches" to specific-layer requirement.)
- `-1.5`: direct hands-on experience with the core build problem; founder has built or operated something materially similar.

**TC Boundary block** (V9.20 NEW) — explicit forbidden-phrase list preventing drift into Risk 3 / Main Bottleneck territory: "execution risk", "completion risk", "binding constraint", "make or break", "the build is the bottleneck", "the founder may struggle", "without X this fails", "rises or falls on". TC describes what makes the build hard and how the founder's profile changes that difficulty; does not interpret what that difficulty means for venture success.

**Idea-specific adjustment prose discipline** (V9.20 NEW — Principle 13 cure surface for Stage TC) — `adjustment_explanation` must engage with specific facets of THIS idea, not generic profile labels. Cross-profile variation comes from real founder/idea interaction not artificial randomization. User pattern: ONE stable profile across MANY ideas — same `adjustment_value` may apply across user's session, but `adjustment_explanation` prose must vary per idea or templating compounds across user's lifetime.

**Schema change** (V9.20 NEW) — `explanation` field CUT (was redundant with `base_score_explanation` post-decomposition). 6-field shape:
```
{
  "technical_complexity": {
    "base_score": 7.5,
    "base_score_explanation": "1 sentence naming the build difficulty and matched anchor.",
    "adjustment_value": -0.5,
    "adjustment_explanation": "1 sentence naming the specific profile facet and how it interacts with this idea.",
    "score": 7.0,
    "incremental_note": null
  }
}
```

**incremental_note boundary** (V9.20 NEW) — if the idea has an obvious smaller starting point, name ONE concrete reduced version; otherwise `null`. Must NOT sequence multiple phases, estimate time-to-build, predict outcomes, or recommend whether the founder should take that path.

**Prose length budget** (V9.20 NEW) — 1 sentence per prose field, 3 sentences total maximum.

**3 worked example clusters** (V9.20 NEW) — Cluster 1 measurement perimeter (HIPAA-grade health companion + non-technical PM founder, demonstrating TC stays inside measurement perimeter not Risk 3 territory); Cluster 2 anti-anchor-fixing (legal document automation + paralegal with intermediate coding, demonstrating math must reconcile with prose claims, with explicit BAD example showing 7.0 + (-0.5) ≠ 7.0); Cluster 3 same founder different ideas (hospital procurement operator profile across 3 ideas — hospital procurement workflow dashboard, general B2B SaaS analytics, HIPAA patient-data companion — demonstrating same profile, different idea-specific adjustment prose, different rungs based on real interaction).

**V9.20 calibration patch (same-day, post-Run-1 verification):**

Tightened -1.0 rung definition requiring SPECIFIC layer match (routes general engineering capability to -0.5 explicitly) + compact 4-line boundary examples block demonstrating -0.5 vs -1.0 vs -1.5 across two profile types (B2B SaaS engineer + HIPAA pipeline engineer) + promoted base_score profile-blindness from one ontology sentence to standalone hard rule with self-test heuristic ("would this same idea, evaluated for a different founder, still match this anchor? If the answer depends on the founder, your anchor match is wrong.").

**Verification methodology** — isolated `/api/stage-tc` endpoint at `src/app/api/stage-tc/route.js` (NEW, 108 lines) taking `{idea, profile}` and returning Stage TC output directly without full-pipeline orchestration (~$0.03/call vs ~$0.55/call full pipeline, 20x cheaper / 10x faster). Verification runner `runners/run-v4s29-stage-tc-verification-http.js` (1103 lines, locked gates per Methodology Principle 6) with 2-cohort design: diseased cohort 15 cases × 3 reruns = 45 runs (MAT1/MAT2/MAT3 trios + score-band diversity + edge cases) + cross-profile cohort 5 profiles × 15 ideas = 75 runs (testing same-profile-many-ideas angle variation per Principle 13). Total 120 runs / ~12-18 min wall time / ~$3.50-4 cost.

**Verification results — Run 1 (post-structural-session, pre-calibration-patch):** All hard sentinels PASS — G_TC_ARITHMETIC 100% (was 15% pre-cure), G_TC_LADDER_VALIDITY 100%, G_TC_BASE_RANGE 100%, G_TC_SCHEMA_FIELDS 100%, G_TC_FORBIDDEN_PHRASES 0 hits, G_TC_PROSE_LENGTH 100%; G_TC_MAT1_POSTCURE_SPREAD {6.5, 6.0, 5.5} spread 1.0 monotonic; G_TC_WITHIN_RERUN_STABILITY 14/15 = 93.3%; Profile 3 beginner floor 100% expected match; cross-profile prose overlap <5% across all profiles (anti-templating works). Calibration findings exposed: P1 senior tech engineer 33.3% match (14/15 at -1.0+, inflation pattern), P5 healthtech engineer 6.7% match (15/15 at -1.0+, worse inflation), base_score drift across profiles for 7/15 ideas.

**Verification results — Run 2 (post-calibration-patch):** All sentinels held (arithmetic 100%, schema 100%, forbidden phrases 0 hits, MAT1 trio identical, beginner floor 100%); calibration improvements: P5 6.7% → 33.3% (+26.6pp dramatic — 6 cases moved to -0.5), P1 33.3% → 46.7% (+13.4pp modest — 2 cases moved to -0.5), P2 hospital CFO 73.3% → 80.0% (+6.7pp), P4 restaurant manager 80% → 80% held, P3 beginner 100% held; base_score drift unchanged 7/15 (standalone profile-blindness rule had zero observable effect — known residual); within-rerun stability 14/15 (different case shifted post-patch, no net change); specific facet rate 86.5% → 89.0% (still below 90% soft threshold).

**Anchor predicates** (V9.20 updated — legitimately TC's, should not appear elsewhere):

- Anchor citations: "matches the [X] anchor at [Y]" (preserved from V1)
- Engineering challenges named concretely: "HIPAA infrastructure", "real-time safety-critical systems", "fine-tuning workflows", "custom retrieval", "audit trail systems" (preserved from V1)
- Numeric decomposition vocabulary (NEW V9.20): `base_score`, `adjustment_value`, "decomposes to", "base difficulty", "profile adjustment"
- Ladder rung references (NEW V9.20): "-0.5 adjustment", "-1.0 adjustment", "-1.5 adjustment" — explicit rung values appear in prose
- Specific-facet markers (NEW V9.20): "your N years as [role]", "your [specific operational background]", "your [direct technical experience with X]"
- Boundary phrases (NEW V9.20): "directly transfers to", "does not transfer to", "general engineering capability applies but", "specific layer match"
- Incremental starting points: "could start with [simpler version]", "A simpler starting point would be [one concrete reduced version]" (preserved from V1)

**Forbidden predicates** (V9.20 extended — these belong to other surfaces):

- "Buyer access" / "distribution" / "network" / "relationships" → Risk 3 + Main Bottleneck territory (preserved from V1)
- "Market is crowded" / "well-understood market" / "buyer urgency" → MD territory (preserved)
- "Pricing" / "willingness to pay" / "monetization gap" → MO territory (preserved)
- "Defensibility" / "moat" / "incumbent replication" → OR territory (preserved)
- "Founder lacks credibility" / "founder lacks domain access" → Risk 3 territory (preserved)
- "Execution risk" / "completion risk" / "the founder may struggle" → Risk 3 territory (V9.20 NEW)
- "Binding constraint" / "the bottleneck" / "the build is the bottleneck" → Main Bottleneck territory (preserved + extended V9.20)
- "Make or break" / "rises or falls on" / "without X this fails" → Risk 3/Main Bottleneck verdict language (V9.20 NEW)

**Verification anchors for B10b (V9.20 updated):**

- TC explanation must contain at least one anchor citation match (regex: `matches the [a-z\s,/]+anchor`) — preserved from V1
- TC explanation must NOT contain any forbidden predicate from the V9.20-extended list above — extended from V1
- TC schema must have all 6 required fields (`base_score`, `base_score_explanation`, `adjustment_value`, `adjustment_explanation`, `score`, `incremental_note`); must NOT have `explanation` field (cut V9.20) — NEW
- TC arithmetic check: `score === max(1.0, base_score + adjustment_value)` ≥95% of runs — NEW V9.20
- TC ladder validity: `adjustment_value ∈ {0, -0.5, -1.0, -1.5}` 100% of runs — NEW V9.20
- TC base range: `base_score ∈ [3.0, 10.0]` 0.5 increments 100% of runs — NEW V9.20
- TC prose length: max 3 sentences across `base_score_explanation` + `adjustment_explanation` + `incremental_note` — NEW V9.20
- TC same-profile-many-ideas angle variation: 5-gram overlap on `adjustment_explanation` openings <30% per profile across user's session (anti-templating verification anchor for Principle 13) — NEW V9.20
- MAT1 trio post-V9.20: spread ≥1.0 + monotonic ordering (NOTE: B10a canonical values {7.5, 7.0, 6.0} were measured under the V9.1 bug — post-cure values may legitimately differ; only spread + monotonicity enforced going forward) — REVISED V9.20

**Known residuals (V9.20 ship state — partial cure, NOT clean lock):**

- **P1 senior-tech inflation pattern partial:** 12/15 ideas still produce -1.0 for senior B2B SaaS engineer profile against expected -0.5 in many cases (simple wrappers like AI resume reviewer, habit tracker, trade association newsletter). Pattern: model interprets "this product has payment integration" or "this product has API integration" as matching "specific technical layer" for an integration specialist. Calibration patch tightened the rule but did not make "specific" itself tight enough.
- **Base_score profile-drift unresolved:** 7/15 ideas in cross-profile cohort show base_score variation across profiles for the same idea (e.g., AUDIT-MAT2 6.5 / 7.5 / 8.0 across 3 profiles). Calibration patch's standalone profile-blindness block + self-test heuristic had zero observable effect post-Run-2. Two possible interpretations: (a) prompt-rule enforcement insufficient — model reads self-test, acknowledges, then ignores at scoring time; OR (b) calibration matrices contain multiple defensible anchors per idea, profile context shifts which anchor feels strongest — drift is defensible variation, not violation. Uncertainty between interpretations not resolved this session.
- **Specific facet rate 89% soft miss:** 12 prose failures use generic phrasings like "Your intermediate coding skills help with..." or "Your staff engineering experience directly transfers..." that technically reference roles but generically. Same family of issue as P1 inflation.
- **Within-rerun stability 14/15:** different case shifted between Run 1 (AUDIT-MAT2-intermediate flipped 6.5/7) and Run 2 (AUDIT-MAT2-beginner flipped 6.5/5.5). Boundary cases where model is on the fence between two anchors.

**Ship decision** (V9.20): SHIP THE PATCHED VERSION. Strictly better than pre-patch on every metric. Generosity bias direction forgiving (lower TC reads as encouraging not alarming). Known residuals affect quality not correctness. Pre-launch infrastructure exists to revisit post-launch with real user data.

**Status (V9.20):** V9.1 LANDED. Structural cure shipped. Calibration patch shipped. Known residuals documented for B10b consumption and post-launch monitoring. **Future TC calibration revisit possible** if real-user friction surfaces on the documented residuals (P1 inflation, base_score drift). Conditional V9+ amendment shape preserved for that scenario.

---

### 3.2 — Risk 1 (market_category slot)

**Bundle:** V4S28 B1 (S1+S2+S3 — Stage 2c creation).
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage2c.js` → `failure_risks[].slot === "market_category"` → frontend Risks card.
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 2 P2-S1; audit-findings.md Section 2 (lines 182–349).

**MUST own:** *"What market-level, category-level, or competitive pressure could kill this idea — independent of who the founder is?"*

This is the idea-level market risk. Anchored on factors observable from competitor data and category dynamics, not founder profile.

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Trust/adoption territory** (Risk 2's job): if the risk is about user adoption friction, behavior change, or trust requirements, it belongs in Risk 2, not Risk 1.
- **Founder-fit territory** (Risk 3's job): never references the founder's profile, skills, or background. Risk 1 is profile-blind by design (V4S28 B1 architectural lock).
- **Binding constraint territory** (Main Bottleneck's job): Risk 1 names a risk; it does not declare the single binding constraint of the idea.
- **Build territory** (TC's job): never references how hard the product is to build.

**Anchor predicates:**

- Competition language: "incumbent already serves", "category is mature", "competitor [X] dominates"
- Substitution language: "free substitute", "manual workflow alternative", "spreadsheet replacement"
- Category dynamics: "category is shifting", "platform consolidation", "M&A activity"
- LLM substitution risk: "general-purpose LLM can replicate", "single-prompt substitution"
- Lead rotation rule: Risk 1 must NOT begin with a proper noun (locked rule from B1).

**Forbidden predicates:**

- "You" / "your" / "the founder" / direct profile references → Risk 3 territory
- "Trust requires" / "adoption friction" / "behavior change" → Risk 2 territory
- "Hardest technical problem" / "build complexity" → TC territory
- "The binding constraint" / "main bottleneck" → Main Bottleneck territory

**Cross-references allowed:**

- May reference Stage 1 competitor data and competitive landscape findings.
- May reference Stage 2a packets (market_demand and originality packets specifically).
- Must NOT reference profile.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- Risk 1 text must NOT contain "you", "your", or direct profile references (zero tolerance — profile-blindness is architectural).
- Risk 1 should reference at least one specific competitor or category dynamic (not generic "market is competitive").
- Risk 1 should not begin with a proper noun (lead rotation rule from B1).

---

### 3.3 — Risk 2 (trust_adoption slot)

**Bundle:** V4S28 B1.
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage2c.js` → `failure_risks[].slot === "trust_adoption"` → frontend Risks card.
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 2 P2-S1; audit-findings.md Section 2.

**MUST own:** *"What trust, adoption, monetization, or distribution friction could prevent this idea from reaching its users — independent of who the founder is?"*

Risk 2 covers idea-level adoption mechanics: behavior change required, trust-building lag, monetization willingness, distribution friction. Like Risk 1, this is profile-blind.

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Market territory** (Risk 1's job): if the risk is about competitor pressure or category maturity, it belongs in Risk 1.
- **Founder-fit territory** (Risk 3's job): never references the founder. Trust risks here are about *user trust*, not *user trust in the founder specifically*.
- **Binding constraint territory** (Main Bottleneck's job): names a risk, not the gating constraint.
- **Build territory** (TC's job): adoption friction ≠ build complexity.

**Anchor predicates:**

- Trust language: "users need to trust", "regulated decisions", "high-trust domain", "clinical/legal/financial decision-influencing"
- Adoption friction: "behavior change required", "incumbent workflow entrenched", "switching cost"
- Monetization friction: "willingness to pay unproven", "free alternative widely used", "buyer not the user"
- Distribution friction: "two-sided liquidity", "network effect required", "distribution channel saturated"

**Forbidden predicates:**

- "You" / "your" / direct profile references → Risk 3 territory
- "Incumbent dominance" / "category maturity" → Risk 1 territory (note: Risk 2 may reference "incumbent workflow entrenched in user behavior" — that's about user adoption, not market dynamics)
- "Hardest technical problem" → TC territory

**Cross-references allowed:**

- May reference Stage 1 domain risk flags (high-trust domain, marketplace, consumer habit, llm substitution).
- May reference Stage 2a monetization packet evidence.
- Must NOT reference profile.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- Risk 2 text must NOT contain profile references (zero tolerance).
- Risk 2 should reference an adoption/trust/monetization mechanism, not a market-pressure mechanism.

---

### 3.4 — Risk 3 (founder_fit slot)

**Bundle:** V4S28 B1.
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage2c.js` → `failure_risks[].slot === "founder_fit"` → frontend Risks card.
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 2 P2-S1; audit-findings.md Section 2 (P2-S1, lines 306–315).

**MUST own:** *"What founder-execution-fit gap (skill / network / capital / sales / credibility) — outside of technical build difficulty — could block THIS founder from delivering this idea?"*

Risk 3 is the only profile-aware Risk slot. It exists specifically because the audit (Section 5 P5-S2 + Section 2 P2-S1) found that the system had no surface for *non-technical* founder-fit gaps. TC handles technical build difficulty for the founder; Risk 3 handles everything else (network, distribution access, domain credibility, capital runway, sales/conversion experience).

**Archetype enum (locked B1):** A (technical execution gap) / B (buyer access gap) / C (domain credibility gap) / D (capital/runway gap) / E (sales/conversion gap). Archetype A is the rare overlap with TC and only fires when the technical gap is severe enough to be the *primary* execution risk, not just a build-time adjustment.

**STEP 1 PROFILE-DOMAIN MATCH rule:** When the founder's profile matches the idea's required domain (e.g., MAT3-insider — former CFO building a hospital tool), Risk 3 is dropped before archetype evaluation. The result is a Founder-fit case (no founder_fit slot at all), and Main Bottleneck stands alone as idea-intrinsic.

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Technical build difficulty territory** (TC's job): Risk 3 is for *non-technical* execution gaps. If the gap is "founder can't write the code", that's a TC adjustment, not a Risk 3. Archetype A is the limited exception — only when the technical gap is so severe it dominates execution risk.
- **Market risk territory** (Risk 1's job): Risk 3 is profile-specific; Risk 1 is profile-blind. If a risk applies regardless of who the founder is, it belongs in Risk 1.
- **Trust risk territory** (Risk 2's job): "users won't trust this product" is Risk 2; "this founder lacks the credibility users require" is Risk 3 archetype C.
- **Binding constraint territory** (Main Bottleneck's job): Risk 3 names a founder gap; Main Bottleneck names *the* binding constraint of the idea. They may align (Risk 3 archetype B "lacks hospital network" + Main Bottleneck "Buyer access") or layer (Risk 3 archetype A "lacks engineering depth" + Main Bottleneck "Trust/credibility"), but they answer different questions.
- **Build complexity territory** (TC's job): never references anchor examples, hardest engineering challenges, or build difficulty calibration.

**Anchor predicates:**

- Profile-specific language: "you" / "your background" / "your [N years of] experience" — but only as faithful descriptions of the actual profile (per V4S28 B1 P1-S1 rule, no fabricated domain attribution)
- Archetype-specific markers:
  - A: "engineering depth required", "production ML expertise", "specialized infrastructure skills"
  - B: "lacks the buyer network", "no hospital CFO relationships", "no enterprise sales access"
  - C: "lacks domain credibility", "no clinical credentials", "users require expert-level trust"
  - D: "capital runway insufficient", "burn rate exceeds available runway", "fundraising required before execution"
  - E: "lacks outbound sales experience", "no proven conversion motion", "founder-led B2B sales required"

**Forbidden predicates:**

- "Market is crowded" / "category dynamics" → Risk 1 territory
- "Users will not adopt" → Risk 2 territory (Risk 3 is about founder reaching users, not users accepting the product)
- "Matches the [X] anchor at [Y]" → TC territory
- "The binding constraint" / "the bottleneck" → Main Bottleneck territory
- Domain-credibility claims that don't match the profile (V4S28 B1 P1-S1 rule: stem-match against profile.education tokens; no fabricated "your healthcare background" when profile says "healthtech startup").

**Cross-references allowed:**

- Must reference profile faithfully (per B1's P1-S1 stem-match rule).
- May reference idea characteristics that interact with the profile gap.
- Must NOT reference Stage 1 competitor data — that's Risk 1's evidence base.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- Risk 3 must contain a profile reference (either "you/your" or a specific profile fact).
- Risk 3 archetype must be one of A–E (or null for STEP 1 MATCH cases — but in null cases, the slot is dropped entirely).
- Risk 3 archetype must align with text content (archetype B should mention buyer/network/access; archetype C should mention credibility/trust/expertise).
- Profile attribution must pass stem-match against profile.education (B1 P1-S1 rule: no fabricated domain claims).

**V9.19 amendment — Stage 2c C7 archetype selection discipline (May 16, 2026, F23 surgical patch):**

When two archetypes appear to fire for a Risk 3 case, the archetype selection MUST route through (a) C5 per-archetype evidence patterns and (b) Section 1.1 case-truth as fallback. The deprecated soft tiebreaker "pick the one whose binding-constraint resolution unblocks the EARLIEST meaningful validation step" produced non-deterministic selections across reruns because temporal-sequence projection varies stochastically when multiple archetypes plausibly fire.

The new tiebreaker procedure:
1. Compare candidate archetypes against per-archetype evidence patterns in C5 (which already has rich anchors with 24 worked examples for prose composition).
2. Select the archetype whose C5 evidence anchors most directly describe the concrete profile.education ↔ idea-requirement gap in this case.
3. If both archetypes' C5 anchors directly describe the case (pairwise tie), use Section 1.1 case-truth to select the archetype tied to the most verdict-impactful founder-task gap.

**Verification anchors added by V9.19:**

- Pairwise archetype confusion (2-way): MUST resolve deterministically across reruns. Verified empirically: AUDIT-H2 (was A/B/A → now A/A/A), AUDIT-A2 (was A/A/B → now B/B/B) with downstream Stage 3 MB inheriting stability.
- Tri-archetype confusion (3+ way): KNOWN RESIDUAL tracked as F23 residual. Cases with 3+ plausible C5 anchors (AUDIT-M1 A/E/B all plausibly apply) may still produce variance because both the C5 anchor test and the case-truth fallback can wobble when multiple archetypes have valid anchors. Affects boundary cases in MAT trio specifically.
- Cure scope correctly limited to archetype-when-fired, NOT fire-decision-itself. F15 fire/no-fire variance (e.g., AUDIT-MAT3-tech-no-access drop/B/drop) is separate cure surface at C1 substantive-fire criterion, not C7 selection tiebreaker.
- B↔C boundary cases (AUDIT-MAT3-partial B/B/B → B/C/C) are NOT regressions when both archetypes have valid C5 anchors for the case. Both readings are substantively defensible; archetype label is descriptive not factual on true boundary cases.
- Banned-phrase preservation: F23 cure MUST NOT regress F2 ("Building the platform itself drives the timeline"), F17 ("Your N years..." opener), F18 ("is increasingly consolidated") cures. Verified 0/24 hits across all banned patterns post-cure.

**F23 known residual notation:** Tri-archetype confusion logged as known limitation. User-accepted at cure ship: "MAT trio caused me so many errors dude, like the IdeaLoop Core cannot produce single answer in that idea, always reads it differently." Tri-archetype cases are inherently noisy region of the case space — case-specific structural ambiguity, not bug. Future iteration may add explicit tri-pair handling (Option 2 from cure design discussion: add sentence to C7 routing tri-pair cases to Section 1.1 case-truth as primary determinant rather than fallback). Deferred until user-facing impact warrants.

---

### 3.5 — Summary text

**Bundle:** V4S28 B1.
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage2c.js` → `summary` JSON output → frontend Summary card.
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 1 P1-S1, P2-S2; audit-findings.md Section 1 (lines 29–181).

**MUST own:** *"What's the synthesized take across all four metrics + risks + competition, written as a coherent narrative verdict?"*

Summary is the synthesis surface. It is the only surface in the product that is allowed to *combine* content from multiple upstream surfaces. Its job is to integrate, not to introduce new claims.

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Adding new claims**: Summary may not introduce evidence that doesn't appear in the underlying metrics, risks, or competition data.
- **Score territory**: Summary may reference scores, but should not re-justify them — that's the metric explanation's job.
- **Roadmap territory** (Stage 3's job): Summary may not produce a build sequence or phase breakdown.
- **Templated openers**: V4S28 B1 P2-S2 forbids the old "this addresses a real pain point but..." pattern. Each Summary opens differently; templating is structurally suppressed.
- **Section-name leaks** (B1 hygiene rule): never references "Risk 3", "the founder_fit slot", "STEP 1", etc. — these are internal labels.

**Anchor predicates:**

- Verdict language: "this idea is strongest at [X] but weakest at [Y]"
- Synthesis markers: "combining the [X] and [Y] signals", "the central tension is", "the strongest signal is"
- Honest framing per audit: when the idea is structurally weak, the Summary should *say so* — defensible harshness is a product identity choice (audit's "honesty as trust strategy").

**Forbidden predicates:**

- Section-name references: "Risk 1/2/3", "founder_fit", "STEP 1", "slot", "archetype" → these are internal labels
- New evidence not in upstream: any claim that doesn't trace back to a metric explanation, risk, or competitor
- "Phase 1 should be...", "First, build..." → Roadmap territory

**Cross-references allowed:**

- May reference scores and metric findings.
- May reference risks (without naming the slot).
- May reference competitors by name (from Stage 1).
- Must NOT reference internal labels.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- Summary must NOT contain forbidden section-name leaks (regex check from B1's run-b1.js).
- Summary opener must vary across the suite (no templated opener firing in >25% of runs — F3 templating threshold).
- Summary content must trace to upstream data (no fabricated facts).

---

### 3.6 — Main Bottleneck enum + explanation

**Bundle:** V4S28 B3 (S4 — Main Bottleneck).
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage3.js` → `estimates.main_bottleneck` (enum) + `estimates.main_bottleneck_explanation` (text) → frontend Execution Reality chip.
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 4; audit-findings.md Section 4 (lines 503–658).

**MUST own:** *"What is the SINGLE binding constraint that gates this idea — the one thing that, if unsolved, makes everything else moot?"*

Main Bottleneck is the gating-constraint surface. It declares which dimension dominates execution risk, regardless of whether that dimension is technical (Technical build), market-side (Buyer access, Distribution), trust-side (Trust/credibility, Compliance), data-side (Data acquisition), category-side (Category maturation), or specification-side (Specification — sparse-input case only).

**Enum (8 values, locked B3):** Technical build / Buyer access / Trust/credibility / Compliance / Distribution / Data acquisition / Category maturation / Specification.

**Three relational cases (locked Section 4 design):**

- **Alignment** — Risk 3 archetype maps cleanly to Main Bottleneck enum (e.g., archetype B → Buyer access). Both surfaces converge on the same dimension; founder gap matches idea constraint.
- **Layered** — Risk 3 archetype differs from Main Bottleneck enum; both compound (e.g., archetype A "lacks engineering depth" + Main Bottleneck "Compliance" — founder has a build gap AND the idea is gated by compliance regardless).
- **Founder-fit case** — Risk 3 is null (STEP 1 MATCH); Main Bottleneck stands alone as idea-intrinsic.

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Founder-specific gap territory** (Risk 3's job): Main Bottleneck names the *idea's* binding constraint, not the founder's gap. In Founder-fit cases, Main Bottleneck is purely idea-intrinsic. In Alignment/Layered cases, Main Bottleneck still names the gating dimension of the idea, even when Risk 3 names a founder gap that aligns or layers.
- **Build difficulty territory** (TC's job): Main Bottleneck "Technical build" is allowed when build genuinely gates everything else, but the explanation must justify it as a *binding* constraint, not just "this is hard to build."
- **Multiple-constraints territory**: Main Bottleneck names ONE binding constraint. If the idea has multiple equally important constraints, the prompt picks the most binding per the locked priority rule (Compliance > Trust/credibility > others).
- **Risk-listing territory** (Risks' job): the Main Bottleneck explanation is not a list of risks — it justifies *the one* gating constraint.

**Anchor predicates:**

- Binding-constraint language: "gates everything else", "the single biggest blocker", "without solving X, nothing else matters"
- Enum-specific markers per locked Section 4 design:
  - Technical build: "specialized engineering required", "production ML training", "regulated infrastructure"
  - Buyer access: "without reach to [buyer type], nothing matters", "B2B contract gating"
  - Trust/credibility: "users require expert-level trust", "credibility-gated adoption"
  - Compliance: "FDA 510(k) clearance required", "SOC 2 / HIPAA before users sign", regulatory binary gates
  - Distribution: "two-sided liquidity", "network density", "consumer habit formation"
  - Data acquisition: "needs N verified submissions", "cold-start data problem"
  - Category maturation: "category not yet ready", "user education gap", "early-adopter only"
  - Specification: ONLY fires when evidence_strength === "LOW" — sparse-input case

**Color taxonomy (locked B3):** Indigo / Purple / Teal / Slate / Pink / Cyan / Sage / Stone — selected to avoid collision with severity colors (red/amber/blue/green reserved for Difficulty pills, scores, TC, step indicators).

**Forbidden predicates:**

- "Your" / "you" / direct profile references → Risk 3 territory (Main Bottleneck is idea-intrinsic, not profile-specific)
- "Multiple bottlenecks" / "several constraints" → there is ONE binding constraint by design
- "Hardest engineering challenge" / "anchor" → TC territory (unless the binding constraint genuinely IS technical build)

**Cross-references allowed:**

- May reference Stage 1 domain risk flags (high-trust domain, marketplace, etc.).
- May reference Stage 2a packets and Stage 2b scores. [V5.0 correction: "Stage 2b scores" → the MD/MO/OR mechanical-lookup scorer scores; Stage 2b is deleted.]
- Reads Stage 2c output (failure_risks) — sequential pipeline.
- Must NOT reference founder profile beyond what's needed to explain the idea-level constraint.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- Main Bottleneck enum must be one of the 8 locked values.
- Explanation must justify *why this constraint is binding above others* — not just describe the constraint.
- In Founder-fit cases (Risk 3 null), explanation must NOT reference founder gaps.
- In Layered cases (archetype mismatch), explanation must justify why the idea-intrinsic constraint dominates over the founder-specific one.
- TC-first opening rule: the `estimates.explanation` may open with "The technical complexity score of X.X combined with..." ONLY when Main Bottleneck === "Technical build". Outside that case, opening must vary.
- Specification enum fires ONLY when evidence_strength === "LOW".

---

### 3.7 — Execution Reality (duration + difficulty + explanation)

**Bundle:** V4S28 B3 (Section 4 — also covers duration/difficulty/explanation around Main Bottleneck).
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage3.js` → `estimates.duration`, `estimates.difficulty`, `estimates.explanation` → frontend Execution Reality card.
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 4; audit-findings.md Section 4 (lines 503–658).

**MUST own:** *"How long will this take, how hard will it feel, and why — calibrated to the founder's profile and the idea's binding constraint?"*

Execution Reality is the *cost-of-the-journey* surface. Duration and difficulty are the headline numbers; explanation justifies them by tying back to TC, Risk 3 (if present), and Main Bottleneck.

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Plan territory** (Roadmap's job): never produces phase sequencing or build steps. Execution Reality answers *the cost*; Roadmap answers *the sequence*.
- **Verdict territory** (Summary's job): never produces an overall verdict. Execution Reality tells the user the journey cost; whether to take the journey is the Summary's domain.
- **Score-justification territory** (metric explanations' job): may *reference* TC and other metrics, but does not re-justify them.
- **Risk-listing territory** (Risks' job): may reference *the* binding constraint, but does not list risks.

**Sparse-input rule (locked B1, mirrored in B3, enforced upstream by B5):** When evidence_strength === "LOW", duration must be "Cannot estimate until specific workflow is defined", difficulty must be "N/A", and Main Bottleneck must be "Specification".

**Anchor predicates:**

- Duration ranges: "6-8 months", "12-18 months" — calibrated to TC + binding constraint, not to overall score
- Difficulty enum: Easy / Moderate / Hard / Very Hard
- Explanation markers: "calibrated to your [X] background", "the binding [constraint] adds [time] beyond technical build alone"
- Cross-reference markers: "the technical complexity score of X.X", "given the [Main Bottleneck enum] gating", "the [Risk 3 archetype] gap adds [time]"

**Forbidden predicates:**

- "Phase 1 should..." / "First build..." → Roadmap territory
- "This idea is worth pursuing because..." → Summary territory
- "The hardest engineering challenge is..." → TC territory (Execution Reality may reference TC; it does not re-explain TC)

**Cross-references allowed:**

- May reference TC score (numerical) and TC's adjustment commentary.
- May reference Main Bottleneck enum and explanation by name.
- May reference Risk 3 archetype consequences (e.g., "the buyer-access gap adds 4-6 months of relationship-building").
- Must NOT reference Risks 1 or 2 — those are profile-blind market/trust risks, not execution-time inputs.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- Duration must be a parseable range (or "Cannot estimate..." in sparse case).
- Difficulty must be one of {Easy, Moderate, Hard, Very Hard, N/A}.
- Explanation must reference at least one of: TC score, Main Bottleneck, Risk 3 archetype consequence.
- Explanation opening should vary (not >70% TC-first per audit's templating finding).
- Sparse case: duration === "Cannot estimate...", difficulty === "N/A", Main Bottleneck === "Specification".

---

### 3.8 — OR Explanation (originality output)

**Bundle:** V4S28 B4 (Section 6 P6-S3 — OR actionability hook enforcement). V4S20 originally added a soft "actionability suggestion"; B4 reinstated it as enforced two-element required structure after verification revealed the V4S20 instruction had been dropped (firing in only ~6-8 of 34 audit runs, ~20%).
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage2b.js` → `originality.explanation` JSON output → frontend metric card. Mirrored in Free `prompt.js`.
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 6 P6-S3 lines 936–963; audit-findings.md P6-S3 (lines 960–967).

**MUST own:** *"How original is this idea (rubric-level justification of the OR score), AND what is the single most realistic change that would make it more defensible against incumbent replication — or honest acknowledgment that no realistic defensibility path exists?"*

The surface answers the originality question through a required two-element structure:
1. **Rubric-level justification** — which OR band the score maps to and why, grounded in OR packet evidence (Pro) or competitor search context (Free).
2. **Defensibility-improvement suggestion** — one sentence identifying the single most realistic change that would strengthen defensibility against incumbent replication, OR the honest exit clause "No realistic defensibility path exists against incumbents with this approach." when no realistic path is identifiable.

The defensibility-improvement suggestion must be:
- Specific (named data source, named capability, named integration — not generic directions)
- Realistic (not "invent a new technology")
- Tied to THIS idea's structural situation

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **MD territory** (market_demand's job): never claims about market size, buyer urgency, or demand signals as part of the originality assessment.
- **MO territory** (monetization's job): never claims about pricing or willingness-to-pay.
- **TC territory** (technical_complexity's job): never claims about build difficulty as part of OR rubric.
- **Risk 3 territory** (founder_fit slot's job): never references the founder's profile, skills, or background. OR is profile-blind; the defensibility hook must be tied to THIS idea's situation, not to THIS founder's fit.
- **Main Bottleneck territory** (Stage 3's job): the hook is a defensibility-improvement suggestion, not a binding-constraint declaration. Even when the suggested moat path aligns with the eventual Main Bottleneck, the OR explanation must not claim it's THE binding constraint.

**Anchor predicates:**

- Rubric-level justification: "Score [N], rubric level [N-N] — [reason citing competitor evidence]"
- Action verbs for specific improvement: "building", "creating", "establishing", "developing", "constructing", "integrating", "aggregating", "curating", "sourcing", "accumulating"
- Specificity markers (must accompany action verbs): named data sources ("dataset of legal contract patterns across 10,000+ matters"), named integrations ("EHR workflow integration with Epic"), named network mechanisms ("two-sided liquidity between hospital procurement officers and vetted vendors"), proper nouns of specific companies/systems
- Honest exit clause (verbatim): "No realistic defensibility path exists against incumbents with this approach."

**Forbidden predicates (anti-generic guardrail):**

- "Consider building proprietary data" without naming the source
- "Create network effects" without naming the two-sided mechanism
- "Deepen integrations" without naming the integration
- "Create a competitive moat" without naming the moat type
- These phrases are forbidden regardless of context UNLESS followed by a specific named target on the same sentence.

**Cross-references allowed:**

- May reference Stage 1 competitor data (named competitors).
- May reference OR packet evidence (Pro pipeline) — replication difficulty, competitor overlap, evidence_strength signals from the OR packet specifically.
- Must NOT reference Stage 2c output, founder profile, or Main Bottleneck.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- OR explanation must contain a final sentence that is either: (A) a specific defensibility-improvement suggestion with action verb + named target, OR (B) the honest exit clause verbatim or close paraphrase.
- OR explanation must NOT end with a forbidden generic phrase without a specific named target.
- OR explanation must contain a rubric-level justification (band reference + competitor-evidence reason) before the actionability hook.
- Free pipeline must produce identical structural shape to Pro (V4S28 B4 verification confirmed parity); only the grounding depth differs (Pro uses evidence packets, Free uses competitor search context).
- Hook firing rate ≥ 95% across any verification suite (B4 baseline: 17/17 = 100% on 17-run suite).

---

### 3.9 — Evidence Strength (evidence_strength output)

> **[V5.0 / V9.28 PRODUCER CORRECTION — producer moved Stage 2b → Stage 2a (recorded May 29 2026; flagged in the June 4 2026 dead-as-live audit).** The §3.9 + §3.9a text below names **Stage 2b** (`prompt-stage2b.js`) as the Pro-pipeline producer of `evidence_strength` and `thin_dimensions`. **Stage 2b is DELETED.** Under V5.0, `evidence_strength` (with `thin_dimensions` inside it) is emitted by **Stage 2a directly** (`prompt-stage2a.js`, Option A — per the V9.28 amendment in the header log above), and the assembly-layer strip/restore in `analyze-pro/route.js` now wraps the **Stage 2a** output. **Read every "Stage 2b" in §3.9 + §3.9a as "Stage 2a" for the current producer.** Unchanged: LOW-only generation, the 3-value enum (`target_user`/`use_case`/`mechanism`), the strip-before-Stage-2c/3 invariant + restore-at-final-assembly, frontend rendering, and Free-pipeline `prompt.js` parity. The G1-LONG-1500W `level: null` follow-up (below) should be re-verified against Stage 2a. The original Stage-2b wording is retained as pre-V5.0 historical record per append-only discipline; THIS banner is the authoritative current-state producer fact.]**

**Bundle:** V4S28 B4 (Section 8 — Confidence rename + warning-channel reframe). Replaces the V4S20-era `confidence_level` field, which the audit identified as decorative and load-bearing for the F/P inversion (Section 8 finding F: Standard pipeline produced HIGH 100%, Pro produced HIGH 35% — simpler pipeline appearing more trustworthy). The rename + Option Z MEDIUM rule + asymmetric display (HIGH hidden) addresses all three issues. **B5 (April 27, 2026) confirmed the LOW-trigger conditions are now physically enforced upstream at Stage 2a — see contract section 3.10.** **B9 v2 (May 1, 2026) rewrote the MEDIUM contract to fire only on input-actionable richness gaps (closing the B8-surfaced live observation that Stage 2b mis-fired MEDIUM on well-specified inputs with evidence-side reasons like "buyer urgency under-evidenced") and added iteration discipline preventing goalposts-moving across re-evaluations of the same input.**
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage2b.js` (Pro) + `prompt.js` (Free) → `evaluation.evidence_strength` JSON output → asymmetric frontend rendering (HIGH silent default, MEDIUM/LOW rendered as blue-tinted callout per B8 lock).
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 8 lines 1116–1148; audit-findings.md Section 8 (lines 1008–1148); V4S28-B9-CLOSURE.md (B9 v2 contract rewrite + iteration discipline).

**MUST own:** *"Does the user's input have a specific, addressable gap that — if filled with one or two sentences — would materially sharpen the evaluation?"* (Post-B9 v2 narrowing — was previously a broader three-signal warning channel covering evidence sufficiency + market legibility + input specificity; B9 v2 tightened to input-actionable richness gaps only because the broader scope produced category errors where the model surfaced evidence-side gaps the user could not act on.)

The field is a constructive nudge for the user, not an integrity hedge or a confidence claim about the evaluation.

The level is one of HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW with locked semantics:

- **HIGH** — the input contains the user-addressable details needed to ground the evaluation. **Default state for well-formed inputs. Silent in UI** (no callout below metric bars). External market uncertainty, thin search evidence, or lack of validation may still reduce metric scores via anti-inflation rules, but they do NOT lower this field by themselves. (B9 v2 locked: HIGH does not absorb evidence-side or market-side uncertainty as a defensive lower-confidence signal.)

- **MEDIUM** — the input is evaluable, but at least one specific user-addressable detail is materially absent. If multiple gaps exist, the reason names the SINGLE most important one — the one whose addition would most change the evaluation. The user receives one nudge, not a checklist. Frontend rendering: blue-tinted callout below metric bars with locked heading "This score could be sharper" + body using `evidence_strength.reason` text directly.

- **LOW** — the input is not safely evaluable because fundamental product specification is absent, contradictory, or unstable. Concretely: one or more of {target user, workflow, core feature} is missing, OR multiple incompatible products are described in one input, OR target/workflow/feature are stated but cannot be reconciled into a single coherent product. Rare after the upstream Haiku gate (§3.13) which catches most thin inputs; LOW functions as defense-in-depth. Triggers Specification + N/A cascade in Stage 2c (sparse-input rule) + Stage 3 (Specification main_bottleneck + "Cannot estimate..." duration + "N/A" difficulty). Frontend rendering: blue-tinted callout with locked heading "Want a real read on this idea?" + body explaining the early-read state + 2-3 dynamic bullets driven by Stage 2b's `thin_dimensions` array (see §3.9a).

**LOW-trigger conditions (B4 semantic, B5 upstream-enforced, B9 v2 expanded):** LOW fires when ANY of the original three sparse-input triggers from Stage 2a is met (word count < 20, contradictory or ambiguous scope, pure-narrative dump without product specification) OR when the input describes multiple incompatible products in one input OR when target/workflow/feature are stated but cannot be reconciled into a single coherent product. Stage 2a (B5 contract section 3.10) physically produces thin packets under any of these conditions; Stage 2b's evidence_strength = LOW assignment then reflects the upstream packet shape rather than re-deriving the trigger condition independently.

**MEDIUM materiality test (B9 v2 locked):** Before firing MEDIUM, the model applies: *"If the user added one or two sentences addressing this gap, would the score, monetization read, competitor interpretation, or execution path change in a meaningful way?"* If YES → MEDIUM is appropriate, name the single most important gap. If NO → use HIGH; the detail is nice-to-have, not material.

**Iteration discipline rule (B9 v2 locked) — DO NOT MOVE GOALPOSTS:**

MEDIUM is a one-shot nudge, not a checklist. MEDIUM should fire only when one specific user-addressable gap is so material that the evaluation would be meaningfully less useful or potentially misleading without it. If several details are merely underdeveloped, use HIGH and let the metric explanations carry the nuance. The model does NOT surface a sequence of progressively smaller gaps across repeated evaluations of the same input shape.

Once the idea contains reasonable treatment of buyer/user clarity, pricing/monetization, distribution, competitive positioning, and product mechanism, prefer HIGH unless one remaining ambiguity would materially distort the evaluation. The model has no memory of prior evaluations — this rule applies to the absolute state of the current input, not to what was previously flagged.

**DO NOT ASK THE USER TO PROVE THE MARKET (B9 v2 locked, critical predicate):**

Do NOT use MEDIUM to ask the user to prove demand, urgency, willingness to pay, adoption trust, regulatory acceptance, or external validation. Those questions are evaluated by the product analysis itself (MD, MO, OR, failure_risks). MEDIUM only flags missing product/context details the user can state in a sentence.

**Valid MEDIUM reason categories (B9 v2 locked, six categories):**

1. **Pricing model not specified** — per-seat, per-usage, freemium, etc. would lead to different Monetization Potential reads
2. **Buyer not distinguished from user** — who pays for this product is implicit and changes the market demand framing
3. **Distribution channel not addressed** — for a category where reach is the binding constraint, the go-to-market path is unstated
4. **Competitive positioning not articulated** — incumbents in this category are obvious, but the differentiation against them is not stated
5. **Product mechanism named but not operationalized** — the input describes WHAT the product helps with but not WHAT IT DOES FIRST to deliver that help; different first-action choices would lead to different evaluations
6. **Target segment too broad** — the evaluation would shift materially depending on which sub-segment is the actual focus

**Invalid MEDIUM reason categories (B9 v2 locked, four categories):**

1. **Evidence-side gaps the user cannot fix** — "buyer urgency is under-evidenced" (search retrieval limitation), "adoption mechanism is unproven" (market/data limitation), "replication barrier unclear because incumbent behavior varies" (evidence interpretation), "external validation lacking" (search-side limitation). These are forbidden under DO-NOT-ASK-USER-TO-PROVE-MARKET.
2. **Risks or market findings that belong in metric explanations** — "trust barrier is high" (belongs in OR or failure_risks), "competition is intense" (belongs in OR explanation), "adoption could be hard" (belongs in MD explanation or failure_risks), "incumbents may copy this" (belongs in OR explanation), "market willingness is uncertain" (belongs in MD explanation). These are real evaluation findings; the score and metric explanations carry them, Evidence Strength does not.
3. **Nice-to-have details that don't materially change the read** — implementation/tech details (UNLESS feasibility or moat depends directly on the implementation approach), geographic scope (UNLESS regulated/local/marketplace domain where geography materially changes evaluation), stage of progress (concept vs MVP vs in-market — useful context but rarely material to scoring), founder background details (handled by TC, not Evidence Strength).
4. **Generic hedging** — "some aspects could be stronger", "reasonably established category", "generally well-understood but not fully certain", "clear market with some uncertainty".

**Optional affected-section naming (B9 v2 locked, lightly-required):**

When the connection is natural and brief, MEDIUM reasons mention the specific metric or section whose interpretation would shift if the user filled the gap. Use human-readable names: "Market Demand", "Monetization Potential", "Originality", "Technical Complexity", "Roadmap", "Competitor read". Do NOT use abbreviations (MD, MO, OR, TC). Mention at most two affected areas; most reasons should name one. If adding the section reference makes the reason longer or more mechanical, omit it — the callout should remain elegant.

This is *optional/lightly-required* — not every MEDIUM reason must include a section reference. The B9 v2 verification observed ~80% organic compliance with this pattern across 15 MEDIUM cases without forcing it. Forcing every reason to include a section creates audit-error feel.

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Idea outcomes territory:** never produces reasoning that reads as confidence ABOUT the idea ("this idea will likely succeed/fail" / "the evaluation is reliable" / "confident in this idea"). The field reports an input-actionable richness gap, not an authority claim about outcomes.
- **Evidence-side or market-side uncertainty (B9 v2 hard rule):** never surfaces gaps the user cannot fix — search thinness, market category illegibility, lack of external validation, incumbent-behavior interpretation variance. These silently bias scores down via anti-inflation rules; they do NOT trigger an Evidence Strength flag.
- **Risks territory** (failure_risks' job): never enumerates risks. The reason is one sentence about an input-actionable richness gap, not a risk inventory.
- **Metric-explanation territory:** never re-justifies any specific metric score. Evidence Strength is a meta-signal about input richness, not about any one metric's number.
- **Founder-fit territory** (Risk 3's job): never references the founder's specific gaps as part of the evidence-quality assessment.
- **Main Bottleneck territory** (Stage 3's job): never declares a binding constraint. Even when LOW evidence_strength fires Specification main_bottleneck downstream, the Evidence Strength reason itself is about input richness, not about constraint identification.

**Anchor predicates (B9 v2 locked):**

- HIGH: silent default; reason text optional in JSON output, may say "input contains user-addressable details needed to ground the evaluation" or similar — but HIGH renders no callout in UI so the reason is essentially internal.
- MEDIUM: input-actionable gap markers — "[X] not specified", "[X] not articulated", "[X] not addressed", "[X] not distinguished from [Y]", "[X] not operationalized", "[X] too broad", "would lead to different [Section] reads", "would change the [Section] framing", "would shift the [Section]". Optional section names: Market Demand / Monetization Potential / Originality / Technical Complexity / Roadmap / Competitor read.
- LOW: input-quality markers — "input is too vague", "input is too thin", "no specific [workflows/features/buyer type] identified", "specification gap", "contradictory scope", "undefined core mechanism", "lacks specificity", "no defined [product/workflow/buyer/target]", "multiple incompatible products described", "target/workflow/feature cannot be reconciled".

**Forbidden predicates (B9 v2 locked):**

- **Evidence-side phrasings (closed via B9 v2 rewrite):** "buyer urgency is under-evidenced", "adoption mechanism is unproven", "replication barrier unclear because incumbent behavior varies", "external validation lacking", "no signal of [user behavior]", "no data on [adoption pattern]", "search shows", "incumbent behavior varies", "evidence base varies", "competitor evidence is thin/sparse/limited".
- **Risk-as-MEDIUM phrasings:** "trust barrier is high", "competition is intense", "adoption could be hard", "incumbents may copy this", "market willingness is uncertain". These belong in metric explanations or failure_risks.
- **Idea-confidence patterns:** "this idea will likely succeed/fail", "the evaluation is reliable", "confident in this idea/the score/the evaluation", "the score is reliable/trustworthy/accurate".
- **Generic hedging:** "clear market with some uncertainty", "reasonably established category", "some aspects could be stronger", "generally well-understood but not fully certain".
- **Founder-specific references on any level:** "your background", "your domain access" — Evidence Strength is profile-blind by architecture.
- **Risk inventory:** "risks include X, Y, Z" — that's failure_risks' job.
- **Section-name abbreviations:** "MO", "MD", "OR", "TC" in user-facing reason text. Use human-readable names only.

**Cross-references allowed:**

- May reference Stage 1 competitor data quality (competitor density, evidence_strength of individual competitors).
- May reference Stage 2a packet quality (e.g., "MO packet is sparse" without naming the packet structure).
- Stage 2c sparse-input rule reads `evidence_strength === "LOW"` as the trigger condition.
- Stage 3 Specification enum reads `evidence_strength === "LOW"` as the trigger condition.
- Tradeoffs prompt reads `evidence_strength` field from each side's evaluation in compare flow.
- Delta prompt reads `evidence_strength` field from parent + child evaluations in delta flow.
- Frontend rendering (V4S28 B8 lock, May 1, 2026): C-2 layout in EvaluationView. HIGH renders as default summary card with no callout (silent). MEDIUM renders blue-tinted callout below the metric bars with locked heading "This score could be sharper" + body using `evidence_strength.reason` text directly. LOW renders blue-tinted callout with locked heading "Want a real read on this idea?" + body explaining the early-read state + 2-3 dynamic bullets driven by Stage 2b's `thin_dimensions` array (see §3.9a) + falls back to all 3 static prompts if thin_dimensions is missing/empty. Header chip switches: HIGH/MEDIUM display "OVERALL X.X /10"; LOW displays "EARLY READ X.X /10". TC visually separated by "EXECUTION CONTEXT · NOT IN THE OVERALL" centered divider in prose card.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- Schema: `evidence_strength` field present with `level` ∈ {HIGH, MEDIUM, LOW} and non-empty `reason`. Zero `confidence_level` references in src/ (verified post-B4 deploy: clean).
- HIGH reasons must NOT contain idea-confidence patterns.
- MEDIUM reasons must contain at least one input-actionable gap marker AND must NOT contain forbidden evidence-side / risk-as-MEDIUM / generic-hedging patterns. (B9 v2 hard requirement.)
- LOW reasons must reference input quality (vagueness, contradiction, missing specification, multi-product, irreconcilable target/workflow/feature).
- Cross-stage: when LOW fires, Stage 2c produces the sparse-input cascade (specification gap framing, no inferred-product evaluation) AND Stage 3 produces Specification main_bottleneck + "Cannot estimate..." duration + "N/A" difficulty. End-to-end propagation must hold (B5 verified 17/17 LOW cases).
- Frontend (B8 lock): HIGH cases produce no callout below the metric bars. MEDIUM cases produce blue-tinted callout with "This score could be sharper" + reason text. LOW cases produce blue-tinted callout with "Want a real read on this idea?" + 2-3 thin_dimensions-driven bullets (or all 3 fallback prompts if thin_dimensions empty/missing). Header chip "EARLY READ" replaces "OVERALL" only on LOW.
- B4 verification baseline: 17/17 design-faithful across 17-run suite, T1-T8 thresholds all clean.
- B5 verification baseline (April 27, 2026): 27-run suite confirms LOW-trigger expansion (contradictory scope + bare-narrative) fires correctly with cross-stage cascade intact.
- B8 manual UI verification (May 1, 2026): HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW states render correctly on production; math verified live (5.5/4.5/4.0 MD/MO/OR → 4.7 Overall, matches new α formula); color boundaries render at correct thresholds.
- **B9 v2 verification baseline (May 1, 2026):** 38-run comprehensive runner across 5 passes, all 8 gated thresholds PASS — T1 G1 HIGH precision 5/6 = 83%, T2 G2 MEDIUM recall 6/8 = 75%, T3 G3 regression precision 5/5 = 100% (bug pattern fully eliminated), T4 evidence-side leakage 0/15 = 0%, T5 generic hedging 0/15 = 0%, T6 materiality phrasing 15/15 = 100%, T7 iteration goalposts 2/3 chains clean (one defensible fire on genuinely vague mechanism), T8 length-MEDIUM correlation PASS. Free vs Pro parity 3/3 match. Pricing dominance 80% of MEDIUMs flagged as observational watch item (not a contract violation — every individual fire correctly identifies real input-side absence; structurally driven by casual-input shape, not model defect or templating). Test-runner: `run-b9.js` v2 with expanded T6 materiality regex (16 patterns covering "would [verb]", "changes/affects/shifts the [section]", "is/are/but not [stated/articulated/specified/operationalized]", "incumbents like X already provide", and human-readable section names directly).
- **G1-LONG-1500W silent failure** (open follow-up): Stage 2b returns `level: null` on dense 1500+ word inputs even after max_tokens 4096 → 8192 bump. Not a contract violation but a structural reliability issue. Schema validation should surface controlled fallback (default to HIGH-silent + log incident) instead of null. Tracked as separate technical follow-up.
