### 3.9a — thin_dimensions UI Metadata Sub-Contract

> **[Producer note: the Pro producer of this field is now Stage 2a, not Stage 2b — see the V5.0/V9.28 PRODUCER CORRECTION banner at §3.9. Stage-2b references in this sub-contract are pre-V5.0 historical.]**

**Bundle:** V4S28 B8 (Section 8 frontend asymmetric Evidence Strength rendering — LOW callout dynamic bullets).
**Lives in:** Both Pro and Free pipelines (Free parity LANDED May 4, 2026 — B9 thin_dimensions hygiene commit). Pro: generated as terminal field inside `evidence_strength` by Stage 2b prompt (`prompt-stage2b.js`) ONLY when `evidence_strength.level === "LOW"`; stripped at assembly layer by `analyze-pro/route.js` before Stage 2c and Stage 3 see the evaluation object; restored at final assembly time after all Sonnet calls complete. Free: generated as terminal field inside `evidence_strength` by unified prompt (`prompt.js`) ONLY when `evidence_strength.level === "LOW"`; no assembly-layer strip needed (single-call pipeline, no downstream Sonnet call to protect). Both pipelines: persisted via `scoring_json` round-trip on save/load/re-evaluate/branch routes (verified pass-through May 1, 2026); consumed only by EvaluationView's LOW callout bullet rendering; format `string[]` with values from a 3-value enum. Tradeoffs and Delta routes (`compare/tradeoffs/route.js` + `ideas/[id]/delta/route.js`) sanitize thin_dimensions out of evaluation payloads before passing to their respective Sonnet calls — locked design invariant that thin_dimensions MUST NOT propagate to any LLM call beyond the Stage 2b call (Pro) or unified Sonnet call (Free) that emits it.

**Locked design source:** V4S28 B8 design phase (May 1, 2026), Mockup #2 LOW state.

**MUST own:** *"Which input dimensions are missing or unclear in this user's idea — chosen from a fixed 3-value taxonomy — so the LOW callout can render specific actionable prompts instead of generic ones?"*

This is **UI metadata only**. It exists to make the LOW callout's bullets specific to the user's input rather than always showing all three generic prompts. Stage 2b chooses which dimensions are most missing in this particular input; the frontend renders bullets keyed to that choice.

**Locked 3-value enum:**
- `target_user` — renders bullet: "Who exactly is this for? Name the user role, buyer, or situation."
- `workflow` — renders bullet: "What workflow or pain point does it handle? Name the specific job, not just the category."
- `core_feature` — renders bullet: "What does the product actually do first? Name the concrete feature or mechanism."

These three strings are FRONTEND-LOCKED in EvaluationView. Stage 2b ONLY emits the enum keys; it does not generate the bullet text.

**Generation rules (Stage 2b prompt):**
- Generated ONLY when `evidence_strength.level === "LOW"`. HIGH and MEDIUM evaluations omit this field entirely.
- Generated LAST in the JSON output (terminal in `evidence_strength` object) to prevent influence on prior fields (scores, MEDIUM/LOW reason text).
- Values must come ONLY from the 3-value enum. Any other value is an enum violation.
- Empty array `[]` is a valid output meaning "all three dimensions are missing" — frontend renders all 3 prompts in that case.
- Subset of 1-3 elements is valid. Order matters: bullets render in the order Stage 2b emits them.

**Defense-in-depth invariant:** thin_dimensions is UI-only metadata. It MUST NOT propagate to any LLM call beyond the Stage 2b call that emits it. Three architectural enforcements:

1. **Assembly-layer filter (analyze-pro/route.js):** After Stage 2b parses + TC merges, the field is extracted to `preservedThinDimensions` and stripped from `ev.evidence_strength`. Stage 2c and Stage 3 see only `{level, reason}`. Defensive: also strips if model returns the field on HIGH/MEDIUM. Restored to `ev.evidence_strength.thin_dimensions` at final assembly time after all Sonnet calls complete.
2. **Persistence pass-through:** Save/load/re-evaluate/branch routes write/read `evidence_strength` as a whole object via `scoring_json`. thin_dimensions rides along. No selective field extraction.
3. **Tradeoffs/Delta input sanitation (LANDED May 4, 2026 — B9 thin_dimensions hygiene commit):** Tradeoffs and Delta are separate post-pipeline LLM calls that read the persisted evaluation. They MUST strip thin_dimensions before passing the evaluation object to those prompts. The LLMs ignore the unrecognized field, so it's harmless in practice — but the invariant requires defensive sanitation. Implementation: `compare/tradeoffs/route.js` ships `sanitizeComparisonData()` helper called once before JSON.stringify into Sonnet message; `ideas/[id]/delta/route.js` ships `extractEvidenceStrength` destructure-rest strip pattern (`const { thin_dimensions, ...cleanEvidenceStrength } = es`). Both helpers are non-mutating, defensive against missing/null shapes, and produce identical-shape objects minus the property on HIGH/MEDIUM where field is already absent.

**Anchor predicates (in Stage 2b prompt instructions):** "missing input dimensions", "UI metadata field", "LOW only", "do not let this affect scores", "terminal field in JSON output", "3-value enum: target_user / use_case / mechanism" (V8.1 rename, May 4, 2026 — was target_user / workflow / core_feature in V6/V7; semantic broadening, see §3.13 V8.1 subsection for full rename rationale).

**Forbidden predicates (would constitute drift):**
- Any value outside the 3-value enum (e.g., "buyer", "use case", "tech stack", "monetization") — invents a finer taxonomy.
- Generation on HIGH or MEDIUM — violates the LOW-only rule.
- Generation as non-terminal field — risks influence on prior scoring fields.
- Bullet text generation by Stage 2b — bullet text is frontend-locked; Stage 2b only emits enum keys.

**Cross-references allowed:**
- §3.9 Evidence Strength — thin_dimensions is structurally a sub-field of `evidence_strength`.
- §3.13 Specificity Gate / Haiku layer — same 3-value enum is used for the gate's `missing_elements` field. The two surfaces share a coarse taxonomy by design (so Haiku's gate failure cards and Stage 2b's LOW callout bullets feel like the same vocabulary).

**Free tier parity (LANDED May 4, 2026 — B9 thin_dimensions hygiene commit):** Both Pro and Free pipelines emit thin_dimensions on LOW. Free `prompt.js` ships THIN DIMENSIONS subsection inside EVIDENCE STRENGTH section + thin_dimensions schema slot in JSON STRUCTURE evidence_strength block. No assembly-layer strip needed for Free (single-call pipeline, no downstream Sonnet call to protect). The 3-value enum + UI-only consumption + LOW-only generation rule + EvaluationView fallback behavior are unchanged across both pipelines. Pre-amendment behavior (Free LOW falling back to EvaluationView's all-3-prompts default) is no longer the live state.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**
- Schema (LOW only, both pipelines): `evidence_strength.thin_dimensions` present, type `string[]`, values ⊆ {`target_user`, `use_case`, `mechanism`} (V8.1 rename — was {`target_user`, `workflow`, `core_feature`} in V6/V7).
- Schema (HIGH/MEDIUM, both pipelines): `evidence_strength.thin_dimensions` absent (omitted entirely, not null, not empty array).
- Pro assembly filter: grep `analyze-pro/route.js` for the strip + restore pattern. thin_dimensions NOT visible in Stage 2c or Stage 3 user message constructions.
- Free emission rule: grep `prompt.js` for THIN DIMENSIONS subsection inside EVIDENCE STRENGTH section + thin_dimensions schema slot in JSON STRUCTURE.
- Persistence round-trip (both pipelines): save → load → re-evaluate → branch all preserve thin_dimensions on LOW evaluations.
- Tradeoffs/Delta sanitation (LANDED May 4, 2026 — same B9 commit): grep `compare/tradeoffs/route.js` for `sanitizeComparisonData` helper + grep `ideas/[id]/delta/route.js` for `extractEvidenceStrength` destructure-rest strip — both confirm thin_dimensions stripped before Sonnet call.
- Free/Pro parity at N>10: B10b runs same input on both pipelines, verifies thin_dimensions emission shape matches across the pair when LOW fires (B5/B6 Free/Pro parity verification was at N=4-6, insufficient sample — B10b expansion target).

---

### 3.10 — Stage 2a Packet Sparse-Input Discipline

**Bundle:** V4S28 B5 (Section 6 P6-S5 — MO packet sparse-input discipline mirror + Section 8 P8-S5 — sparse-input trigger expansion).
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage2a.js` (Pro) → three packets (`market_demand`, `monetization`, `originality`) with `admissible_facts` / `strongest_positive` / `strongest_negative` / `unresolved_uncertainty` per packet → consumed by Stage 2b for scoring + evidence_strength assignment. Mirrored in Free `prompt.js` as inline LOW-trigger body bullet (no packet structure; equivalent discipline at unified-prompt scope).
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 6 P6-S5 (lines 1003–1021) + Section 8 P8-S5 (lines 1192–1209); audit-findings.md P6-S5 (lines 975–976) + Section 8 P8-S5 (line 1045).

**MUST own:** *"What evidence is admissible per metric when the user's input is sparse, contradictory, or pure-narrative — and what is explicitly forbidden as evidence under those conditions?"*

Stage 2a is the architectural quarantine layer (V4S9 lock — physical separation of evidence extraction from scoring). Its sparse-input discipline determines what reaches Stage 2b under thin-input conditions. The contract states what packet outputs MUST and MUST NOT contain when any of three sparse-input triggers fires.

**Three sparse-input triggers (locked B5):**
- **TRIGGER 1 — Word count:** the idea description contains fewer than 20 meaningful words (excluding filler like "I want to build" or "an app that"). Origin: V4S20.
- **TRIGGER 2 — Contradictory or ambiguous scope:** the description contains conflicting scope signals — "maybe X or maybe Y" framings, "a tool that does A and also B and also C" without a coherent connecting mechanism, target user shifting mid-description, or core mechanism described inconsistently across the same paragraph. Origin: B5.
- **TRIGGER 3 — Pure-narrative dump:** the description has 20+ words but names no specific product category, workflow, or core feature. Long backstory or motivation without a specifiable product. Origin: B5.

**Counter-example clause (locked B5, methodology-derived hardening):** Trigger 3 does NOT fire when the description names a workflow, even without naming a product category. NC4-class inputs ("Independent gym owners manage member follow-ups, cancellations, and renewal reminders manually across WhatsApp and spreadsheets. I want to help them organize this and prevent churn.") are evaluable — they name a workflow, target user, and pain. Verified in B5 production (NC4 main + 3 reruns + Free parity = 5/5 NOT LOW).

**MUST own per packet under sparse-input trigger:**

- **MD packet** (V4S20 origin, unchanged in B5):
  - User-stated market statistics tagged `[user_claim]`, NOT used as demand evidence
  - Admissible facts limited to competitor objects, domain flags, and idea_description statements
  - 1–2 facts preferred over manufactured 3–5

- **MO packet** (B5 new, mirrors MD's discipline):
  - Admissible facts limited to: domain flags, competitor objects returned by Stage 1 search, and the explicit observation that the user did NOT specify a payment model, pricing approach, or target buyer
  - `strongest_positive` constrained to `[competitor: Name]` or `[domain_flag]` facts
  - `unresolved_uncertainty` MUST name what the user specifically did not specify on monetization (target buyer / payment model / pricing tier / revenue mechanism)

- **OR packet** (V4S20 origin, unchanged in B5):
  - Naturally scores low on unspecified products via rubric ceiling — no new B5-specific discipline added at Stage 2a layer

**Cross-packet verification item 9 (B5 new):** Before finalizing Stage 2a output, verify that under sparse input, the MO packet's `strongest_positive` does not rely on inferred-pricing or domain-convention claims rather than `[competitor: Name]` or `[domain_flag]` evidence. Belt-and-suspenders for the in-packet rule.

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Adding new metrics or packets:** the three packets (MD/MO/OR) are the architecturally locked surface (V4S9). No new packets under sparse input.
- **Producing scores:** Stage 2a is sorter, not analyst (V4S9 lock). Sparse-input discipline produces thin packets, not low scores.
- **Making interpretation claims:** Stage 2b is the analyst. Stage 2a's sparse-input rule outputs admissible-fact lists with structural constraints, not score implications.
- **Refusing to extract:** sparse rule produces thin packets with explicit gap-naming, not refusals (V4S20 lock — "the goal is NOT to refuse to evaluate thin inputs").
- **MO inferred-pricing claims** (B5-specific):
  - "Dental practices already pay for software" without `[competitor: Name]` corroboration
  - "Hospital systems have IT budgets" without `[competitor: Name]` corroboration
  - "Banks afford to spend on AI tools" without `[competitor: Name]` corroboration
  - Any willingness-to-pay assertion derived from buyer-type or domain conventions rather than competitor evidence

**Anchor predicates (Stage 2a packet outputs under sparse trigger):**

- Explicit non-specification facts: "User did not specify [target buyer / payment model / pricing approach / revenue mechanism / use case / features]"
- Source tags: `[domain_flag: ...]` or `[competitor: Name]` on admissible_facts (NOT `[idea_description]` for inferred specifics)
- "Inferred match due to sparse input" notes on competitor extractions where the match is approximate
- 1–2 admissible_facts per packet (not padded to 5)
- `unresolved_uncertainty` naming specific missing information per packet:
  - MD: "User did not specify target buyer, use case, features, or revenue model"
  - MO: "User did not specify target buyer, payment model, pricing tier, or revenue mechanism"
  - OR: vague-product framing (rubric-driven low score follows)

**Forbidden predicates (Stage 2a packet outputs under sparse trigger):**

- Domain-convention pricing inferences: "[Domain] already pays for [category]", "[Buyer type] has budgets for [category]", "[Industry] willing to pay for [solution category]"
- Inferred specific products, feature sets, workflows, or target users the user did not state
- 3+ admissible_facts when input is genuinely thin (padding violation)
- Judgment language: "strong demand", "weak defensibility", "significant friction", "clear opportunity" — preserved from V4S9 lock
- `[idea_description]` source tag on facts that are model inferences rather than user statements

**Cross-references allowed:**

- Stage 2a packets feed Stage 2b directly. Stage 2b reads packet contents to score and assign evidence_strength.
- Sparse-input trigger firing → Stage 2b's evidence_strength = LOW (per contract section 3.9 LOW-trigger conditions) → cascades to Stage 2c sparse summary + Stage 3 Specification main_bottleneck + "Cannot estimate" duration + "N/A" difficulty.
- Cross-packet verification item 9 (Stage 2a internal) checks for MO inferred-pricing in `strongest_positive`. Operates within Stage 2a only.
- Stage 2a is profile-blind (V4S9 architectural lock — profile is TC's exclusive territory). Sparse-input discipline does not introduce profile reads.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- Under any sparse-input trigger, MO packet `strongest_positive` must cite `[competitor: Name]` or `[domain_flag]` only — never inferred-pricing claims (regex: `MO_INFERRED_PRICING` from run-b5.js). Manual review distinguishes confirmed violations from gap-naming language ("the input does not specify whether dental practices would pay for this product" is acceptable; "dental practices already pay for software" is not).
- Under any sparse-input trigger, MO packet `unresolved_uncertainty` must name unspecified monetization aspects: target buyer, payment model, pricing tier, or revenue mechanism.
- Counter-example boundary: NC4-class inputs (problem-first with workflow + target user named) must NOT trigger sparse rule. Verified in B5 production (NC4 + 3 reruns: 4/4 MEDIUM with Buyer access bottleneck; FREE-NC4: HIGH with Buyer access bottleneck — counter-example holds across pipelines).
- Cross-stage propagation: when sparse-input trigger fires → evidence_strength = LOW → Stage 2c sparse summary → Stage 3 Specification + N/A cascade. End-to-end propagation must hold. B5 verified 17/17 LOW cases produced clean cascade.
- Variance stability: same input × multiple reruns at temperature 0 must produce same evidence_strength.level (no expanded-trigger bimodality). B5 verified 12/12 stable across 3 sources × 4 runs each (MD1 LOW×4, BN1 LOW×4, NC4 MEDIUM×4).
- Free pipeline parity: Free `prompt.js` LOW-trigger body bullet must produce same evidence_strength outcome as Pro Stage 2a packet discipline on equivalent inputs. B5 verified 2/2 (FREE-SP-DENTAL = LOW; FREE-NC4 = HIGH).

**B5 verification baseline (April 27, 2026):**

27-run targeted suite (run-b5.js + rescore-b5.js). 8/8 thresholds clean. Strike count 0. Detector enumeration uses Narrative Contract V3 §3.10 anchor predicates as source of truth.
- T1 (MO sparse discipline) — 5/5 LOW with clean MO packets, zero `MO_INFERRED_PRICING` violations across all 5 sparse cases.
- T2 (MD1-class contradictory) — 3/3 design-faithful LOW + 1 design-faithful MEDIUM (MD-MULTI test-case authoring miss; case has coherent connecting mechanism, doesn't fit Trigger 2 contradictory-scope criterion. Per B3 + B4 meta-lesson: when runner reports failure, FIRST re-read locked design before treating as model issue).
- T3 (bare-narrative) — 3/3 LOW.
- T4 (negative control + NC4 boundary) — 4/4 NOT LOW. Counter-example for Trigger 3 working in production.
- T5 (cross-stage propagation) — 17/17 LOW cases produced clean Specification + "Cannot estimate" + N/A cascade.
- T6 (Option Z MEDIUM compliance, B4 regression) — 8/8 specific concrete gaps named, zero generic-hedging.
- T7 (variance stability) — 12/12 stable across reruns.
- T8 (Free parity) — 2/2.

**Why Stage 2a is in this contract list but not in the section 4 matrix:**

The section 4 matrix tracks user-facing interpretation surfaces. Stage 2a packets are internal evidence-extraction outputs that the user never sees directly — their visibility is through downstream effects on Stage 2b scores, Stage 2c summary, and Stage 3 cascade. The packet discipline is an architectural contract (governing what can flow into the user-facing surfaces), not itself a user-content contract. Including Stage 2a as section 3.10 documents the discipline; not adding it to section 4 maintains the matrix's user-facing scope.

---

### 3.11 — How-It-Compares (Stage 1 landscape outputs)

**Bundle:** V4S28 B6 (Section 11 P11-S1 + P11-S2 + S9 carryover).
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage1.js` (Pro) → `competition.landscape_analysis` + `competition.differentiation` + `competition.entry_barriers` JSON fields → frontend How-It-Compares card. Mirrored in Free `prompt.js` as `competition.summary` + `competition.differentiation` (Free schema lacks separate `landscape_analysis` and `entry_barriers`).
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 11 (lines 1594–1722) + Section 11 P11-S1 / P11-S2 / S9 carryover; audit-findings.md Section 11 (lines 1437–1539).

**MUST own:** *"What does the surrounding competitive landscape look like — incumbents, recent activity, entry barriers — described factually without judging whether the user should enter it?"*

This surface answers the *factual landscape* question. Stage 1 reports what exists. Stage 2b decides what it means for this idea (via MD/MO/OR scores + Evidence Strength). Stage 2c synthesizes verdict (via Summary + Risks). The boundary between Stage 1's "report what exists" and Stage 2b's "judge what it means" is load-bearing — when Stage 1 drifts into market-accessibility judgment, downstream stages have nothing left to add.

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Market accessibility judgment** (Stage 2b's job): never claims that the market is "crowded," "promising," "open," "closed," or that there is "room for" / "opportunity for" / "clear demand" / "window is closing." Forbidden in direct, inverted ("less crowded"), softened ("relatively open"), and comparative ("not as competitive") forms. Describing what exists is correct. Characterizing whether entry is viable, easier, or harder is a Stage 2b concern.
- **Score implications** (Stage 2b's job): never says the landscape implies a low MD or that defensibility is weak.
- **Founder-fit judgment** (Risk 3 / Main Bottleneck's job): never assesses whether the user can succeed in this landscape. Profile-blind landscape mapping only.
- **Timing-judgment language** (forbidden everywhere): "fast-moving," "catching up fast," "market is heating up," "momentum is building," "race against," "closing window." Factual recency reports are allowed and required when search surfaces dated activity ("Counterforce Health launched in March 2025") — but the interpretation of timing is forbidden.
- **Evidence quality assessment** (Evidence Strength's job): never comments on whether the evaluation is grounded; the data_source field reports retrieval status factually but does not interpret it.

**Anchor predicates** (legitimately Stage 1's, should not appear elsewhere as primary content):

- Maturity descriptors stated factually: "established players including [X, Y, Z]," "category exists with multiple incumbents," "active development with N entrants in the past 6 months"
- Recent-activity dated facts (S9 carryover): "[Company] launched in [Month Year]," "[Company] announced [feature] in [Quarter Year]," "Three new entrants have emerged in the past 6 months"
- Provisional-framing template (under sparse trigger only): "Category inferred from limited input; search executed against [X] as the closest match"
- Provisional language for category-specific claims under sparse trigger: "if the intended category is [X]," "assuming [X] is the target space," "should the user instead mean [Y]"
- Entry-barrier category names without judgment: "trust," "regulation," "data moat," "network effects," "switching costs," "distribution," "capital"

**Forbidden predicates** (these belong to other surfaces):

- "crowded" / "less crowded" / "uncrowded" → Stage 2b territory (market-accessibility judgment)
- "promising" / "less promising" / "somewhat promising" → Stage 2b territory
- "highly competitive" / "less competitive" / "not very competitive" / "fairly competitive" → Stage 2b territory
- "clear demand" / "no demand" → Stage 2b territory
- "opportunity for" / "room for" → Stage 2b territory
- "open market" / "closed market" / "open category" / "closed space" → Stage 2b territory
- "window is closing" / "shrinking window" / "fast-moving market" / "catching up fast" / "heating up" → forbidden everywhere (timing judgment)
- "the user should enter" / "this is a good opportunity" → Stage 2c Summary territory (and forbidden as outcome prediction even there)
- Profile-aware judgments: "this founder is well-positioned," "the user lacks domain access" → Stage 2c Risk 3 territory; Stage 1 is profile-blind by V4S28 B6 architectural lock

**Cross-references allowed:**

- May cite competitors by canonical name (per Stage 1's naming convention rules).
- May reference the data_source field factually (verified vs llm_generated) — this is retrieval status reporting, not interpretation.
- Should NOT reference user profile, founder fit, or downstream score reasoning. Stage 1's job ends at landscape facts.
- When sparse-input rule fires, the provisional opener references the inferred category — this is internal to Stage 1's landscape framing, not a cross-reference to another surface.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- Forbidden-term scan on Stage 1 fields (`landscape_analysis` + `differentiation` + `entry_barriers` on Pro; `differentiation` + `summary` on Free): zero matches across the 9-term forbidden list (direct, inverted, comparative, softened forms). Verbatim list: "crowded" / "promising" / "highly competitive" / "clear demand" / "opportunity for" / "room for" / "window is closing" / "open|closed [market|space|category]" plus inverted forms.
- Sparse-input cases must produce the provisional-framing opener regardless of how confidently search returned a category match. Trigger 1 (sub-20-word) was the most fragile case during B6 verification and required strengthening (worked example + MANDATORY directive added). Verification: SP-DENTAL / SP-PETS / MD1 / BN1 must open with the locked template.
- Counter-example boundary: NC4-class inputs (problem-first with workflow + target user named) must NOT produce provisional framing in landscape_analysis. Verified in B6 production (NC4 + reruns + NC1 well-specified all clean).
- Temporal anchoring (S9 carryover): when search results contain dated incumbent activity, dates appear in landscape_analysis factually; no timing-judgment phrases (forbidden patterns: "window is closing" / "fast-moving" / etc.).
- Free pipeline parity: same forbidden-term discipline applies to differentiation + summary fields on Free. Metric explanation fields (MD, MO, OR, TC) are exempt — friction language ("crowded incumbents") is legitimate scoring vocabulary in metric explanations per the score-explanation consistency rule.

**B6 verification baseline (April 28, 2026):**

25-run targeted suite (run-b6.js + post-fix rerun). Headline results:
- Trigger 1 framing (SP-DENTAL, SP-PETS): 2/2 produce locked opener post-fix (was 0/2 pre-fix).
- Trigger 2 + 3 framing (MD1 family, BN1 family): 100% produce locked opener.
- MAT1 trio competitor list Jaccard similarity post-fix: 0.88 mean (Phase 0 baseline 0.38; profile-strip working).
- Forbidden-term leak rate: 1/25 = 4% (under 5% gate per locked plan; pre-B6 audit baseline was 8.8%).
- B5 regression check: MD1 still LOW + Specification cascade, NC4 still NOT LOW, SP-DENTAL still no MO_INFERRED_PRICING. Stage 2a profile strip (B6 Path A) did not disturb B5's locked behavior.

### 3.12 — Stage 1 Profile-Blindness (architectural discipline)

**Bundle:** V4S28 B6 (Section 12 P12-S1 — strip profile from Stage 1 + B6 Path A finding — strip profile from Stage 2a + B4 Change 4 fold-in — strip profile from Stage 2b).
**Lives in:** `prompt-stage1.js` (system prompt + internal_build classification rule + explicit no-profile rule) + `analyze-pro/route.js` (Stage 1 / Stage 2a / Stage 2b user message construction). Mirrored in Free `prompt.js` as competitor-selection guidance bullet (Free single-call architecture cannot fully isolate; partial-fix pattern locked).
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3.md Section 12 P12-S1 (lines 1737–1846); audit-findings.md Section 12 (lines 1551–1680).

**MUST own:** *"Profile-aware reasoning enters the pipeline at exactly three locations — Stage TC (scoring), Stage 2c Risk 3 founder_fit (synthesis), and Stage 3 Main Bottleneck explanation (roadmap). Every other stage is profile-blind by architectural design."*

This is an architectural discipline contract analogous to section 3.10 — it governs flow of information, not user-facing content. Profile entering profile-blind stages contaminates downstream outputs even when no prompt rule explicitly reads it (the model can hedge or align tone implicitly). The architectural fix is to physically remove profile from the input at those stages, not to add prompt-level rules saying "do not use profile."

**Profile injection map (post-B6, locked architecture):**

| Stage | Profile injected? | Reason |
|---|---|---|
| Stage 1 (landscape) | NO | Landscape mapping is profile-blind. "Which competitors are relevant to this founder" is not Stage 1's question — it's Risk 3 / Main Bottleneck's question. |
| Stage 2a (evidence packets) | NO | V4S9 quarantine — Stage 2a is the architectural quarantine layer; physical separation of evidence extraction from scoring. NarrativeContract V3 §3.10 locked this. B6 Path A finding closed the route-level injection bug. |
| Stage 2b (scoring MD/MO/OR) | NO | MD/MO/OR are idea-property scores per V4S9 lock. Profile influence on these scores creates the "profile leak" failure mode the audit identified (P6-S1, P8-S2). B6 fold-in of B4 Change 4 closed the route-level injection bug. |
| Stage TC (scoring TC) | YES | TC is the only profile-aware scored metric per V4S10–V4S11 isolation lock. Receives profile by design; isolated to its own Sonnet call so it cannot contaminate other stages. |
| Stage 2c (Risk 3 + Summary) | YES | Risk 3 founder_fit slot owns profile-aware execution gaps (B1 lock). Summary may reference Risk 3's content, which carries profile context. |
| Stage 3 (Main Bottleneck + Roadmap) | YES | Main Bottleneck explanation reads founder fit from Risk 3 archetype (B3 lock). Roadmap may calibrate to founder context. |

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Adding profile reads to profile-blind stages**: any future prompt edit to Stage 1 / Stage 2a / Stage 2b that introduces profile reasoning is a contract violation regardless of how the rule is phrased ("consider founder background" / "given the user's domain experience" / etc.). The architecture is route-level; prompt-level workarounds defeat the architectural lock.
- **Removing profile from profile-aware stages**: TC, Risk 3, and Main Bottleneck explanation must continue to receive profile. Removing it would break locked features (TC adjustment math, archetype detection, founder-fit cross-reference).
- **Conditional profile injection**: no "inject profile only when [condition]" patterns. The profile injection map is binary per stage — either always or never.

**Anchor predicates (route-level, code-side):**

- Pro route (`analyze-pro/route.js`): exactly 4 references to `userProfile` template variable in the file — const definition + Stage TC user message + Stage 2c user message + Stage 3 user message. Stage 1 + Stage 2a + Stage 2b user message constructions do not interpolate `userProfile`.
- Stage 1 prompt (`prompt-stage1.js`): system prompt opens with "The user will give you their AI product idea. You do not receive or reason about user profile in this stage." Includes explicit `=== PROFILE-BLINDNESS ===` block stating profile-aware judgments are out of scope for the stage.
- Stage 2a prompt (`prompt-stage2a.js`): system prompt opens with input contract description that lists "A user's AI product idea" + "Competition evidence from a prior stage" — does not list profile. Includes statement that Stage 2a is profile-blind by V4S9 quarantine.
- Free prompt (`prompt.js`): COMPETITION SECTION DISCIPLINE block contains competitor-selection guidance that reasons from idea's target buyer type and domain, not from user profile. Free's single-call architecture cannot fully isolate; partial-fix pattern is the locked acceptable state for Free.

**Forbidden predicates (route-level + prompt-level):**

- Pro route: `userProfile` interpolation in Stage 1 / Stage 2a / Stage 2b user message templates. Pre-B6 the Pro route had injection in Stage 1 (line 186 area), Stage 2a (line 245 area), and Stage 2b (line 313 area). B6 atomically removed all three.
- Stage 1 prompt: any classification rule reading profile (e.g., the pre-B6 internal_build rule that triggered on founder profile). Replacement post-B6 reasons from buyer's organization type and domain, not founder profile.
- Stage 2a prompt: any rule reading profile. The vestigial "and their profile" reference in input contract description was removed in B6.

**Cross-references allowed:**

- TC, Stage 2c Risk 3, and Stage 3 Main Bottleneck explanation freely reference profile in their own outputs per their locked contracts (3.1, 3.4, 3.6).
- Stage 1's `internal_build` competitor classification reasons about the *target buyer's* technical capacity (idea-derived), not the founder's. This is buyer-anchoring per the B6 rewrite — distinct from profile-awareness.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- Static grep gate (pre-commit, not runner): `grep -n "userProfile" src/app/api/analyze-pro/route.js` returns exactly 4 hits at the locked locations (const + Stage TC + Stage 2c + Stage 3). Zero hits in Stage 1 / Stage 2a / Stage 2b user message constructions.
- Static grep gate: `grep -rn "and their profile" src/lib/services/prompt-stage1.js src/lib/services/prompt-stage2a.js` returns zero hits.
- Cross-profile variance shape (MAT-trio test): same idea × multiple founder profiles produces near-identical Stage 1 competitor lists (Jaccard ≥0.50, B6 baseline 0.88) and tight MD/MO/OR score spreads (≤1.5 each), with TC score variance unbounded (TC IS profile-aware; TC variance reflects working profile-awareness, not contract violation).
- internal_build buyer-anchoring: same idea × multiple founder profiles produces stable internal_build presence (either all profiles fire or none — no founder-skill flip). B6 verification: MAT1 trio + IB-SMB clear-negative all 0/0/0/0 internal_build for legal doc automation + dental SMB (correctly NOT firing on small/non-technical buyer types). Pre-B6 audit baseline: MAT1 Beginner=0, Intermediate=1, Senior=1 (founder-skill flip).
- Haiku keyword extractor (`src/lib/services/keywords.js`): function signature `extractKeywords(ideaText)` accepts only idea text; verified module-level in B6 (no profile parameter, no profile reach). Audit's MAT2/MAT3 identical-keywords data corroborates.

**B6 verification baseline (April 28, 2026):**

- Pro route grep gate: 4/4 hits in expected locations, 0/0 in profile-blind stages.
- Prompt grep gate: 0/0 stale "and their profile" references.
- MAT1 trio competitor Jaccard: 0.88 mean (Phase 0 baseline 0.38).
- internal_build cross-profile stability: 0/0/0 across MAT1 trio.
- internal_build clear-negative: 0 on IB-SMB (solo dentists).
- B5 regression hold: MD1 still LOW + cascade, NC4 still NOT LOW, SP-DENTAL still no MO_INFERRED_PRICING (Stage 2a strip did not disturb B5's locked behavior).

### 3.13 — Specificity Gate / Haiku Layer (architectural discipline)

**Bundle:** V4S28 B7 (Section 13 / Item 7 — upstream sparse-input detection at the Haiku keyword extractor).
**Lives in:** `keywords.js` (Haiku-layer specificity check + JSON output contract) + `analyze-pro/route.js` + `analyze/route.js` (halt logic on FAIL — emit `complete` SSE event with gate payload, close stream, return).
**Locked design source:** execution-plan-v4-3-4.md Section 13 (lines 1888–2061); audit-findings.md Section 13 / Item 7 (lines 1681–1820).

**MUST own:** *"Is the input specific enough to enable honest evaluation, or so underspecified that any evaluation would be a coherent report on a category we picked rather than the idea the user meant?"*

This is an architectural discipline contract analogous to sections 3.10 (Stage 2a packet sparse-input) and 3.12 (Stage 1 profile-blindness). It governs flow of information into the pipeline, not user-facing content. Lives in section 3 only, not in the section 4 user-facing matrix.

The gate is the **upstream root-cause primary fix for Cross-Cut #2** (sparse-input premature category commitment). Five defensive layers (Stage 1 §3.11, Stage 2a §3.10, Stage 2b §3.9 Evidence Strength, Stage 2c sparse summary + risks, Stage 3 §3.6 Specification cascade) catch sparse inputs that slip through the gate. The gate is addition, not replacement.

**Output contract (JSON, post-B7):**

| Branch | Shape |
|---|---|
| PASS | `{ keywords: [k1, k2, k3, k4, k5], githubQuery1, githubQuery2, serperQuery1, serperQuery2 }` |
| FAIL | `{ specificity_insufficient: true, missing_elements: [...], message: "..." }` |

**Three triggers (locked Section 13 lock, mirroring B5 §3.10 + B6 §3.11):**

- **Trigger 1 — Word count:** fewer than 20 meaningful words AND no specific product category, workflow, or core feature is named
- **Trigger 2 — Contradictory or ambiguous scope:** conflicting scope signals — "maybe X or Y" framings, target user shifting mid-description, multiple unconnected functions, mixed enterprise/consumer framing
- **Trigger 3 — Pure-narrative dump:** 20+ words but reads as narrative description without naming what the product does

**Counter-example clause (B5/B6 carryover, locked):** problem-first inputs that name target user + workflow + concrete pain (NC4-class) MUST NOT fire the gate. Verified by gym-owners + dental-equivalent rows in the Haiku prompt's example matrix.

**Calibration discipline — DEFAULT TO PASS (with qualifier):** default to PASS only when the product, workflow, or feature is actually named in the input. Imaginability ≠ specificity. False rejects are user-facing harm; false accepts are graceful degradation (defensive layers catch borderline cases).

**MUST own:**

- The specificity-gate decision (whether to halt the pipeline or continue)
- The `missing_elements` coarse 3-value enum: `target_user`, `workflow`, `core_feature` — never finer taxonomies
- The static `message` text attached server-side on FAIL responses (canonical, not customized per input)

**MUST NOT drift into:**

- **Replacing defensive layers:** the gate is upstream addition, not replacement. Stage 1 §3.11 sparse-input rule, Stage 2a §3.10 packet discipline, Stage 2b §3.9 LOW evidence_strength, Stage 2c sparse summary, Stage 3 §3.6 Specification cascade ALL continue to fire on borderline inputs that pass the gate. Any future change that makes downstream layers conditional on the gate's PASS/FAIL is a contract violation.
- **Inventing finer `missing_elements` taxonomies:** no `category_conflict`, `monetization`, `pricing`, `domain` slots. The 3-value enum is the locked surface.
- **Profile-aware decisions:** the gate is profile-blind by architectural lock (mirrors §3.12). Function signature `extractKeywords(ideaText)` accepts only idea text — no profile parameter. Any future change introducing profile awareness at this layer is a contract violation.
- **Halting on parse/network errors:** the fallback path returns crude keywords (PASS-shape) when the Haiku call itself errors. Only successful Haiku FAIL responses fire the gate. A Haiku outage degrades to crude keywords, never halts.
- **Customizing message text per input:** the message is canonical and attached server-side in `keywords.js`. Haiku returns only the structural signal (`specificity_insufficient: true` + `missing_elements`). Per-case customization of message text is a contract violation — cards do user-facing work, not the message field.

**Anchor predicates (output JSON — code-side):**

- Output JSON parses to either `{ specificity_insufficient: true, missing_elements: [...], message: "..." }` (FAIL) or `{ keywords: [...] }` (PASS)
- `missing_elements` array contains only values from the locked enum: `target_user`, `workflow`, `core_feature`
- `missing_elements` is non-empty when `specificity_insufficient` is `true`
- Pipeline halts on FAIL — the SSE event sequence is exactly `keywords_start` → `complete`; no `keywords_done`, no `search_start`, no Stage 1/2/3 events post-gate
- Function signature `extractKeywords(ideaText)` accepts only idea text (no profile parameter, verified module-level in B6 §3.12 and B7)
- Pre-B7 baseline (audit + Phase 0): keywords are profile-blind across MAT2/MAT3 — confirmed not affected by profile injection, since profile is never passed to the Haiku call

**Forbidden predicates (output JSON):**

- `missing_elements` containing values outside the 3-value enum
- Empty `missing_elements` array on FAIL responses
- `specificity_insufficient: true` on inputs that name target user + workflow + core feature (false reject = user harm)
- Module-level signature changes that introduce a profile parameter
- Static prompt rules at the gate that read profile context (the gate is content-rules-only at the Haiku prompt; profile is architecturally unavailable)

**Cross-references allowed:**

- Gate is architecturally **upstream** of all five defensive layers. Gate's PASS does not signal "this input is fully specified" — it signals "specific enough to enter the pipeline." Defensive layers catch borderline cases that pass the gate.
- Gate's FAIL halts the pipeline before any other stage runs — no downstream contamination possible on FAIL.
- Gate's failure mode (parse/network error) degrades to PASS, not halt — defense-in-depth principle applies inversely (the gate fails open to defensive layers, not closed to user harm).
- Free pipeline parity locked by architecture: both routes call the same `extractKeywords` module, so gate decision is identical regardless of route.

**Verification anchors for B10b:**

- 15-case targeted runner (`run-b7.js`): 8 FAIL cases distributed across three triggers (3 + 2 + 3) + 5 sparse-but-specific PASS counter-examples (DENTIST-PA, SHOPIFY-OPT, SMB-ACC, NC4-GYM, NC4-DENTAL) + 2 well-formed PASS controls (LAW-FIRM-DOC, NC1-CUSTOMS).
- T1 (False reject rate): **0% strict** target — Section 13 lock, "false rejects are user-facing harm." Detector: PASS input received `specificity_insufficient: true`.
- T2 (False accept rate): **≤ 12.5%** target — Section 13 default-to-PASS allows slack since defensive layers catch. Detector: FAIL input received PASS-shape response.
- Coarse-enum compliance check on FAIL cases: `missing_elements` array contains only `target_user` / `workflow` / `core_feature`. Detector: array intersection with the 3-value enum equals the array itself.
- Non-empty `missing_elements` on FAIL: array length ≥ 1.
- Latency observation: median + p95 + max captured per run; no threshold (Haiku call adds ~200ms vs. pre-B7 baseline).

**B7 verification baseline (April 28, 2026):**

15-run `run-b7.js` suite via Free pipeline SSE. All four files in atomic single commit (`keywords.js` + both routes + frontend already shipped pre-runner per B7 Path A frontend-then-backend sequence).

| Threshold | Result | Locked target |
|---|---|---|
| T1 — False rejects | **0/7** (0.0%) | 0% strict |
| T2 — False accepts | **0/8** (0.0%) | ≤12.5% |
| Coarse-enum compliance | **100%** all FAIL cases | 100% |
| Non-empty `missing_elements` on FAIL | **100%** all FAIL cases | 100% |
| Counter-example boundary (NC4-class) | **2/2 PASS** (NC4-GYM + NC4-DENTAL) | 2/2 |
| Latency | median 952ms, p95 1138ms, max 1399ms | observational |

Strike count: **0**. Locked design fired correctly on first run; no prompt patches needed.

**Emergent property — discriminating `missing_elements` (B7 verification surfaced):**

Haiku returns only the genuinely absent slots per case, not always all three. Examples from B7 run:

- SP1 ("tool for dentists to save time") → `["workflow", "core_feature"]` — target_user "dentists" IS named
- SP-PETS ("app for pet owners that's helpful") → `["workflow", "core_feature"]` — target_user "pet owners" IS named
- MD-SHIFTING ("...does scheduling and also chat and also note-taking") → `["target_user", "core_feature"]` — workflow IS named (multiple, but named)
- SP-MINIMAL, MD-MULTI, FAKE-SPECIFIC, BN cases → all three slots flagged (everything genuinely missing)

**Implication for the user-facing UI:** the `SpecificityGate` component (B7 frontend) renders only the cards for slots Haiku flagged. SP1 produces a 2-card layout (workflow + core_feature) instead of 3. The grid auto-collapses based on `cardsToShow.length`. This is the locked design behavior; B7 verification confirmed Haiku is discriminating enough to make per-case rendering meaningfully different from per-domain rendering.

**Cross-bundle interaction notes:**

- Gate is upstream of Stage 1 (§3.11 How-It-Compares) — sparse inputs that slip through the gate (Trigger 1 default-to-PASS edge cases) hit Stage 1's provisional-framing rule. Defense-in-depth: gate + §3.11 both fire on borderline inputs.
- Gate is upstream of Stage 2a (§3.10 packet sparse-input) — same defense-in-depth applies. Stage 2a's three-trigger discipline activates on inputs that pass the gate but exhibit sparse signals downstream.
- Gate's FAIL response halts before Stage TC runs — no TC scoring on FAIL. This is intentional: TC requires evaluable input; un-evaluable input shouldn't produce a TC score (which would then need explanation).
- Gate's PASS response carries no signal downstream beyond the keyword set + queries — no `is_sparse` flag propagates. Defensive layers re-detect sparseness independently. This is the "defense-in-depth" architectural choice locked in B7's design discussion (Q2 from handoff).

**B9 v2 Haiku gate UX overhaul (May 1, 2026, locked):**

B9 v2 added user-facing UX discipline to the gate's FAIL state. Backend behavior (Haiku call, JSON output contract, halt logic, profile-blindness, defense-in-depth) UNCHANGED — all B7 anchor predicates and forbidden predicates above remain authoritative. The B9 v2 additions are frontend rendering behaviors that lock how the FAIL state appears to the user.

**Always-show-3-cards layout (locked):** The `SpecificityGate` component renders all three slot cards (target_user / workflow / core_feature) on every FAIL render, regardless of which slots Haiku flagged. Slots Haiku marked as missing render with their colored top border (Pink #993556 light / #ED93B1 dark for target_user; Teal #0F6E56 / #5DCAA5 for workflow; Purple #534AB7 / #AFA9EC for core_feature) + suggestion text. Slots Haiku did NOT mark as missing render with a green check + slot name + "Covered" label at 0.65 opacity. The B7 emergent discriminating-`missing_elements` behavior at the Haiku layer is preserved (gate still returns only genuinely absent slots) — but the frontend now renders the full 3-slot picture so the user sees which pieces they have AND which they're missing, not just what's missing.

This was a deliberate B9 v2 reframe: the prior B7-locked behavior of rendering only flagged slots in 2-card layouts (SP1 → workflow + core_feature) created a "moving goalposts" perception when users iterated — they'd add what was asked, see new cards appear, feel the bar was shifting. Always-show-3 makes the contract visible upfront.

**Complete-example footer (locked):** Below the 3-card grid, render a static example phrase showing what a fully-specified input looks like: *"AI scheduling assistant for dental receptionists that drafts patient follow-ups."* This example is canonical and renders on every FAIL state regardless of which slots are missing. Purpose: anchor the user's mental model of what "specific enough" means without forcing them to read prose explanation.

**3-way conditional gate header (locked, based on missing slot count):**

- **3 missing slots OR 0 missing (defensive fallback):** *"Let's sharpen this before we evaluate."*
- **2 missing slots:** *"Getting closer — two more pieces, then we can evaluate this clearly."*
- **1 missing slot:** *"Almost there — one more piece, then we can evaluate this clearly."*

The progression acknowledges user progress instead of repeating the same neutral header on every iteration. Re-fire after the user adds detail and triggers gate again displays the appropriate progress-aware copy based on the new missing-slot count.

**Subhead reframed around evaluation integrity (locked):**

- **First-fire subhead:** *"To evaluate honestly, we need enough detail to know which product you mean."*
- **Re-fire subhead (1 or 2 missing):** *"Each piece helps us ground the analysis in the product you actually mean."*

Both phrasings frame the gate as protecting evaluation quality, NOT as judging the user's input quality. The forbidden phrasings the B9 v2 redesign closed: "specific enough", "more detail needed", "your input is missing", anything that reads as input-side criticism rather than analysis-side preparation.

**No-credit copy state-aware (locked):** Below the eval counter when the gate is active: *"No credit used — analysis only starts once we can evaluate the idea clearly."* The phrase "specific enough" is forbidden in this string (B9 v2 closure decision — drops user-judgment framing).

**Gate persistence rule (locked, post-B9 v2 — closes the mid-keystroke disappear bug):**

The gate UI persists across textarea keystrokes. Once `specificityGate` state is set (Haiku returned FAIL on Analyze button press), it does NOT clear on subsequent keystroke events in the textarea. The forbidden behavior, removed in B9 v2: any `onChange` handler that contains `if (specificityGate) setSpecificityGate(null)` or equivalent. The previous B7 behavior cleared gate state mid-keystroke, making the suggestion vanish exactly when the user was acting on it.

The gate state clears only on:
- Next gate result (subsequent Analyze button press returns either PASS — clears cleanly — or new FAIL — replaces with new state)
- Page navigation away from the input screen
- Explicit user action that resets the form (e.g., "Start over" if implemented)

**Live detection deferred (post-V4S28 polish surface):**

Debounced background re-checks of slot status as the user types — would fire ~3-5 Haiku calls per gate session and update card states in real-time. Considered during B9 v2 design but deferred per ChatGPT critique on "haunted UI" risk if not implemented carefully. Locked design spec for future implementation:

- Activation only after first gate fire (not on every input session)
- Latest-response-only via abort controller (older requests' results discarded)
- No spinners (avoids "the AI is thinking about my input" anxiety)
- Stop checking once gate state shows all slots covered (don't re-check on continued typing)
- Show extracted value on green cards (truncated/sanitized — "AI scheduling tool for receptionists" → green check on target_user shows "receptionists")

Cost projection ~$5/mo at scale. Defer until after Paddle wired up; not B10a-blocking.

**B9 v2 Haiku UX verification baseline (May 1, 2026):**

Manual smoke test (per B7 standing discipline that gate UX is visual verification, not statistical): 5 cases tested live on production — sparse-1-slot input, sparse-2-slot input, sparse-3-slot input, well-formed PASS input, mid-keystroke persistence test. All five cases verified design-faithful. Gate persistence bug closed. Progress-aware copy fires correctly per missing-slot count. Always-show-3 layout renders correctly. Complete-example footer renders below cards.

**Cross-references to B9 v2 §3.9 amendments:** Gate's FAIL message no longer carries any reference to "specific enough" — that phrasing was a B7 carryover from the era when Evidence Strength's MEDIUM was framed as input-specificity assessment. B9 v2's §3.9 narrowed MEDIUM to input-actionable richness gaps; correspondingly, the gate FAIL state now uses evaluation-integrity framing ("we can evaluate the idea clearly") rather than user-judgment framing ("specific enough"). The two surfaces' user-facing language is now consistent.

**V8.1 Haiku gate calibration revisit (May 4, 2026, locked):**

V8.1 amends §3.13 to address a calibration mismatch surfaced during B9 thin_dimensions hygiene smoke testing (May 4, 2026). A 100+ word restaurant manager input with target_user named, three concrete workflows (inventory + loyalty + scheduling), and three concrete features (POS alerts + email campaigns + shift swapping) was gated. The B7 calibration drifted toward answering "is this a single coherent product?" when the locked design intent (Section 13) was "did the user give us enough to evaluate?" V8.1 closes that drift through three architectural changes: (a) recalibration of the pass criterion + slot semantic frame at the prompt layer; (b) system-wide rename of the slot enum to better-frame names; (c) a deterministic post-FAIL rescue layer at the code layer for a known Haiku structural blindspot. The contract surface — three slots filled with concrete content → PASS — is unchanged at the principle level; what changed is the implementation that enforces it.

**(a) Recalibration: Option A pass criterion (locked).** Slot presence dominates. Multi-product framing is NOT a failure condition. PASS when target_user, use_case, and mechanism are concretely named — even if input is brief, conversational, multi-product, imperfect, contains typos, hedged language, or backstory preamble. FAIL only when the input cannot anchor a target_user / use_case / mechanism reading (imaginability ≠ specificity — the model picking a plausible interpretation does not satisfy the slot; the user must have named it). Word-count thresholds dropped entirely — replaced by a generic-benefit-language guardrail that catches verb-object phrases like "save time", "improve productivity", "help businesses grow" as concrete-action insufficient.

**(b) Slot semantic rename (locked):** target_user RETAINED with prompt clarification (adoption unit, not necessarily literal payer — students/patients/hobbyists count). workflow → **use_case** (broader: job/pain/task/workflow under one umbrella). core_feature → **mechanism** (broader: feature/process/automation/method — how the product intervenes). The rename is purely semantic — the underlying 3-value enum locks at `["target_user", "use_case", "mechanism"]`. Rename surfaces touched: `keywords.js` (SYSTEM_PROMPT + 14-row matrix + JSON schema + validSlots filter), `prompt-stage2b.js` (Pro Stage 2b LOW prose + thin_dimensions enum + JSON schema), `prompt.js` (Free unified prompt LOW prose + worked example + JSON schema), `analyze-pro/route.js` (validEnum array — architectural critical filter), `components.js` (SLOT_ORDER + MISSING_ELEMENT_CARDS keys + card copy: "Who is it for?" / "What does it help with?" / "How does it work?"), `EvaluationView.js` (THIN_DIMENSION_PROMPTS + fallback array), `page.js` (gate-header validKeys + re-eval error string).

**(c) Collapse-pattern rescue layer (locked):** Narrow deterministic post-FAIL override at the code layer (`keywords.js`) for Haiku's known structural blindspot on "for X to verb-object" inputs. Discovery: v3 calibration (full prompt rewrite + matrix expansion) shipped one recalibration miss — Haiku consistently FAILed concise "tool/platform/app for X to verb-object" inputs by flagging mechanism missing, even when the verb-object phrase semantically carried both use_case and mechanism. v2 attempted a prompt-level fix (added "When in doubt, prefer PASS" + collapse principle block); v2 collapsed the sparse-FAIL floor (Block B 8/8 → 0/8) and was reverted via `git revert`. v3 ships v1's prompt unchanged plus a code-layer rescue.

**Rescue conditions (all five must hold for override to fire):**

1. Haiku returned `specificity_insufficient: true`
2. `missing_elements` contains `use_case` OR `mechanism` (or both)
3. `missing_elements` does NOT contain `target_user` (HARD condition — if buyer is missing, never rescue)
4. Input matches `for [target_user] to [verb] [object]` regex pattern with a concrete noun-object after the verb (verb alone is not sufficient — intransitive verbs like "for X to grow" do not satisfy)
5. The captured `[verb] [object]` phrase is NOT in the generic-benefit blocklist

**Generic-benefit blocklist (locked, conservative):**

`save time`, `make work easier`, `make life easier`, `improve productivity`, `be more productive`, `help people`, `help businesses`, `grow faster`, `scale faster`, `improve workflow`, `transform workflows`, `disrupt industry`, `unlock potential`, `increase efficiency`, `be more efficient`. Substring match (case-insensitive). Adding to the blocklist requires explicit rationale; conservative scope is the discipline.

**Pattern coverage scoped narrow (locked):** Rescue matches `for X to verb-object` only — NOT `for X that verb-object` or `for X which verb-object`. Rationale: `that/which` patterns can match too many vague inputs (e.g., "for startups that want to grow faster" — structurally matches but semantically vague). Defer expansion to `that/which` connectors until empirical evidence shows real-user need; current 3 residual fail cases (G2, G11, K1) are acceptable false-rejects per the cost asymmetry principle below.

**Three helper functions (architectural shape):**

- `hasConcreteForToVerbObject(input)` — regex match for the structural pattern, returns the captured action phrase or null. Fail-closed on any ambiguity.
- `isGenericBenefitPhrase(phrase)` — substring check against the 15-entry blocklist.
- `shouldOverrideCollapseFalseReject(input, missingElements)` — top-level orchestrator, all five conditions in order. Cheap conditions (2 + 3) checked first; regex (4) and blocklist (5) only run if those pass.

**Plus `buildRescueKeywords(input)`** — synthesizes a keyword set from the input when the rescue fires (since Haiku's FAIL branch doesn't return keywords). Strips stopwords + short words, takes top 5 unique, builds search query variants. Pads with "software" if input is unusually keyword-poor (defensive — shouldn't happen for inputs that matched the structural pattern).

**Rescue is silent at the UI:** rescued cases produce identical PASS-shape behavior in the rest of the pipeline. No user-facing artifact indicates the rescue fired. This is intentional — the user should experience the rescued case as "the gate worked correctly," not as "the gate caught me but the system fixed it."

**Cost asymmetry principle (locked, surfaced from v2 failure analysis):** False-rejects (legitimate input gated, user sees friendly "sharpen this" panel and edits) are recoverable UX friction. False-passes (slot-empty input passes the gate, Sonnet generates evaluation of nothing, user gets nonsense + we burn tokens) are trust-destroying. The v3 architecture optimizes for failure-mode asymmetry: the rescue layer reduces false-rejects on a common SaaS phrase pattern but is conservatively scoped to never produce false-passes (target_user must be present, generic-benefit verbs blocked, narrow regex scope). When in doubt about extending the rescue, prefer leaving the false-reject in place over taking on false-pass risk.

**Three documented residual false-rejects (acceptable, tracked for B10b):**

- **G2** — *"An idea for a tool that helps freelancers manage their invoicing and payment reminders for late-paying clients"* — `for X that` pattern (rescue is `for X to` only). Haiku flags target_user missing.
- **G11** — *"a platform for restaurants and gyms and salons to handle bookings and reminders and loyalty programs"* — Haiku reads multi-buyer as scattered; rescue cannot fire (target_user is in missing_elements, hard condition fails).
- **K1** — *"Not fully sure yet, but maybe a tool for Etsy sellers that tracks competitor prices and suggests when to adjust their listings"* — `for X that` pattern.

These are recoverable false-rejects (user sees gate panel, edits to a `for X to verb-object` phrasing or adds explicit mechanism wording, retries). Documented as known calibration limitations.

**MUST own (V8.1 update):**

- The slot semantic rename: `target_user` (adoption unit, not literal payer), `use_case` (broader job/pain/task/workflow), `mechanism` (broader feature/process/automation/method).
- The rescue layer's five conditions and conservative scope (the rescue is part of the contract, not a private implementation detail — its scope is locked, expansion requires re-locking).
- The generic-benefit blocklist as the canonical source of "verb-object phrases that do not satisfy mechanism." Future additions require explicit rationale and runner verification.

**MUST NOT drift into (V8.1 additions):**

- **Expanding the rescue regex without verification:** adding `that/which` connectors, weakening the noun-object requirement, removing the target_user-must-be-present hard condition — any of these risks reintroducing the v2 failure mode (sparse-FAIL floor collapse). The v3 lesson: small-scope rescue beats broad-scope teaching.
- **Prompt-level "prefer PASS" meta-instructions:** v2 demonstrated that posture-level prompt directives override the matrix's FAIL teaching globally. Future calibration adjustments belong in (a) example matrix additions or (b) deterministic code-layer rescues, NOT in broad permissive prose at the prompt level.
- **Per-case message customization on rescue:** rescued cases carry no rescue indicator in the response. The PASS-shape return is identical to a Haiku-PASS — the rescue does not surface as user-visible state.

**Anchor predicates (output JSON, V8.1 additions):**

- `missing_elements` array values are exactly from the locked enum `["target_user", "use_case", "mechanism"]` — the V8.1 rename is enforced via the validEnum filter in `analyze-pro/route.js` and `analyze/route.js` (architectural critical filter; defensive against future Haiku output drift).
- Rescue layer is fail-closed: any condition unmet → no override → Haiku's FAIL stands.
- Rescued responses are shape-identical to Haiku-PASS responses (`{ keywords, githubQuery1, githubQuery2, serperQuery1, serperQuery2 }`) — downstream pipeline consumers cannot distinguish rescued from natively-passed.
- `buildRescueKeywords` always returns a 5-keyword PASS-shape (pads with "software" if input is keyword-poor; defensive invariant).

**Forbidden predicates (V8.1 additions):**

- `missing_elements` containing `workflow` or `core_feature` (deprecated names — V8.1 rename enforced).
- Rescue layer firing when `target_user` is in `missing_elements` (hard condition violation).
- Rescue layer firing on a verb-object phrase containing any blocklist substring.
- Empty `keywords` array on rescued response (`buildRescueKeywords` enforces non-empty + 5-element via padding).

**Verification anchors for B10b (V8.1 additions):**

- 71-case + 15-variance regression bank (`run-haiku-calibration.js`): 14 threshold gates covering 14 behavioral classes (bug-trigger canon / sparse-FAIL floor / conversational tone / use_case-mechanism collapse / adoption-unit consumer-or-free / sparse-but-specific / borderline / multi-product / typo / founder-backstory / uncertain-hedged / service-non-software / marketplace / integration-heavy) plus enum compliance / latency / variance / strike-count.
- v3 verification baseline (May 4, 2026, production deploy): 58/61 graded cases correct = 95% pass rate. Block B (sparse-FAIL floor) 8/8 ✓ — no v2-style floor regression. Block D (collapse pattern, the recalibration target) 6/6 ✓ — bug fully closed. ENUM_COMPLIANCE 18/18 ✓ — rename enforced at model-emission layer. VARIANCE 15/15 stable across temp=0 reruns.
- Three documented residual false-rejects (G2, G11, K1) per cost-asymmetry principle.
- Latency p95 ~2400ms (vs B7's 1138ms baseline) — accepted under V8.1 Lock-F (richer prompt semantics worth the latency; gate runs once per Analyze click; below user-perceptual "stuck" threshold). Latency optimization is a candidate for follow-up prompt-slim session, not blocking.

**Cross-references to broader architecture:**

- Gate's PASS-or-rescued response is upstream of all five defensive layers (Stage 1 §3.11 / Stage 2a §3.10 / Stage 2b §3.9 / Stage 2c summary / Stage 3 §3.6). Rescued cases continue to be processed by the defensive layers; if a rescued case lands LOW evidence_strength downstream, that's defense-in-depth working as designed.
- Rescue layer adds zero latency (no extra Haiku call — pure JS check on Haiku's FAIL response).
- Free pipeline parity preserved — both `analyze-pro/route.js` and `analyze/route.js` consume the same `extractKeywords` module containing the rescue layer; rescue fires identically regardless of route.
- V8.1 closes the V7-OPEN-Amendment-3 (live detection deferred) status without action — live detection remains DEFERRED to V8+ post-Paddle session per cost projection (~$5/mo at scale); the v3 rescue layer is a separate architectural surface that does not interact with the live detection deferred spec.

---

## 4. Cross-surface non-overlap matrix

This matrix captures which content type each surface owns exclusively. Each row is a content type; each column is a user-facing interpretation surface. A check (✓) means the surface is the sole owner; an X means it MUST NOT contain that content type.

| Content type | TC | Risk 1 | Risk 2 | Risk 3 | Summary | Main Bottleneck | Execution Reality | OR Explanation | Evidence Strength | How-It-Compares |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Hardest engineering challenge | ✓ | X | X | X | reference-only | reference-only | reference-only | X | X | X |
| Anchor citation | ✓ | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X |
| Profile-aware build adjustment | ✓ | X | X | X | reference-only | X | reference-only | X | X | X |
| Market/category competitive pressure | X | ✓ | X | X | reference-only | reference-only | X | reference-only | X | X |
| Trust/adoption/distribution friction (idea-level) | X | X | ✓ | X | reference-only | reference-only | X | X | X | X |
| Founder-execution-fit gap (non-technical) | X | X | X | ✓ | reference-only | reference-only | reference-only | X | X | X |
| Synthesized verdict across metrics | X | X | X | X | ✓ | X | X | X | X | X |
| Single binding constraint declaration | X | X | X | X | X | ✓ | reference-only | X | X | X |
| Build sequence / phase ordering | X | X | X | X | X | X | X (Roadmap-only) | X | X | X |
| Duration estimate | X | X | X | X | X | X | ✓ | X | X | X |
| Difficulty rating | X | X | X | X | X | X | ✓ | X | X | X |
| Originality rubric justification | X | X | X | X | reference-only | X | X | ✓ | X | X |
| Defensibility-improvement suggestion | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | ✓ | X | X |
| Honest-exit clause (no defensibility path) | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | ✓ | X | X |
| Input-actionable richness gap (single user-addressable detail) | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | ✓ | X |
| Evidence sufficiency / market legibility / input specificity assessment (PRE-B9-V2 — historical) | — | — | — | — | — | — | — | — | (deprecated, see Evidence Strength row above) | — |
| Factual landscape mapping (incumbents, recent activity, entry barriers) | X | reference-only | reference-only | X | reference-only | reference-only | X | reference-only | X | ✓ |
| Market-accessibility judgment ("crowded" / "promising" / "open" / "closed" / etc., direct or inverted) | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X (forbidden in How-It-Compares per B6 contract; allowed only in metric-explanation scoring fields) |
| Timing-judgment phrasing ("window is closing" / "fast-moving" / "heating up") | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X (forbidden everywhere — factual recency dates allowed in How-It-Compares only) |
| Idea-confidence / outcome prediction | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X | X (forbidden everywhere — no surface owns this) |

**Rules for the matrix:**

- **✓ (own)** — this surface is the sole owner of the content type. No other surface may contain it.
- **X (forbid)** — this surface must NOT contain this content type. Belongs elsewhere.
- **reference-only** — this surface may reference the content type by name (e.g., Summary may say "given the Buyer access bottleneck") but must not re-derive or re-justify it.

**Special row — "Idea-confidence / outcome prediction":** Forbidden everywhere. No interpretation surface in the product is allowed to make confidence claims about whether the idea will succeed or fail. This was the V4S20-era Confidence field's primary failure mode (the F/P inversion) and is explicitly architected out of the new Evidence Strength field. If any surface drifts into outcome prediction, that's a contract violation regardless of which surface produced it.

**Note on architectural-discipline contracts (sections 3.10 + 3.12):** Stage 2a packet discipline (3.10) and Stage 1 Profile-Blindness (3.12) are architectural contracts governing flow rather than user-facing content. Their verification anchors operate at the packet-output / route-construction layers (regex detectors + grep gates against code, not cross-surface prose comparison). Including them as section 3 contracts documents the disciplines; not adding them to section 4 maintains the matrix's user-facing scope. B10b's runner consumes their anchor predicates as detector enumeration source-of-truth — for 3.10 the MO packet shape under sparse trigger; for 3.12 the route-level grep gate plus cross-profile variance shape (Jaccard / score spreads / internal_build stability).

The matrix expanded with B6 to add the How-It-Compares column (Stage 1 user-facing landscape). Future expansions: Score Tier Label in V6 with B9, etc.

---

## 5. Update protocol

When a bundle locks design for an interpretation surface or architectural discipline:

1. **Write the surface contract** in this file as a new subsection under section 3 (numbered to match bundle order). Each contract follows the template:
   - MUST own (the unique question)
   - MUST NOT drift into (adjacent surfaces + drift conditions)
   - Anchor predicates (legitimate words/phrases)
   - Forbidden predicates (drift words/phrases)
   - Cross-references allowed (rules for legitimate inter-surface reference)
   - Verification anchors for B10b (programmatic checks)

2. **Update section 4's matrix** with new row(s) for the new surface and column updates for any cross-references the new surface introduces. Architectural disciplines (like Stage 2a in 3.10) that govern flow rather than user-visible content are added to section 3 only, not section 4 — see the note below the matrix.

3. **Increment file version** in the header (V1 → V2 → V3 etc.).

4. **Update Master Reference** with a one-line entry pointing at the new contract version.

5. **Update handoff doc** for next session to include this file in the standard upload set alongside Master Reference + execution plan + audit findings.

The contract is written from the **locked design**, not from verification results. If verification later reveals the implementation didn't match the contract, the fix is a targeted prompt patch on the offending surface — not a contract revision. The contract is the design intent; the verification is the implementation check.

A contract is revised only when the design itself is intentionally changed (e.g., a future bundle decides Main Bottleneck should expand its enum to 9 values — the contract updates to reflect the new design).

---

## 6. B10b connection

B10b (narrative coherence verification) is the planned post-B9 launch gate that consumes this file. The B10b runner will be designed once all surfaces are locked (after B9). This file is what makes that runner possible.

**B10b's three test layers map to contract sections:**

- **Layer 1 — Boundary fidelity (programmatic):** For each surface, check that its output contains its anchor predicates and avoids its forbidden predicates. This catches lexical drift (the prose contains words that belong to another surface's territory).

- **Layer 2 — Non-redundancy (programmatic, cross-surface):** For each pair of surfaces, check that one surface does not contain another surface's anchor predicates beyond the cross-references the contract allows. This catches semantic overlap (two surfaces saying the same thing in different words).

- **Layer 3 — Cumulative narrative (LLM-as-judge + human spot-check):** Reading the surfaces in order (TC → MD/MO/OR explanations → Evidence Strength → Risks → Summary → Main Bottleneck → Execution Reality → Roadmap → Tools), does each surface earn its place by adding new perspective? This is the user-experience truth signal that calibrates whether Layer 1+2 thresholds were calibrated correctly.

**Architectural-discipline contracts (currently 3.10 only):** verified at the packet/extractor layer rather than cross-surface. B10b's runner consumes 3.10's anchor predicates as detector enumeration source-of-truth (MO packet shape under sparse, counter-example boundary, cross-stage propagation). This is the layer that catches "the upstream rule didn't fire" failures, complementary to Layers 1–3 which catch "the user-facing surface drifted" failures.

**Both Layer 1 + Layer 2 detectors will encode assumptions** about what each surface should look like. Per B3's meta-lesson, when B10b reports a contract violation, the FIRST step is re-reading the contract block to confirm the detector encoded the rule correctly — only AFTER that confirmation should the violation be treated as a model issue. The runner is a detector, and detectors can encode wrong expectations.

Bundle launch sequence: B10a (behavioral regression — the existing 34-run regression) and B10b (narrative coherence) both run before launch. Both must pass.

---

## 7. V7 LOCK record + V8 LOCK record

**V7 LOCKED at May 4, 2026** (post-B9 full closure session). **V8 LOCKED at May 4, 2026** (post-V4S28 B10-prep / Haiku gate v3 collapse-pattern rescue session, same day, single tracked Amendment V8.1 LANDED).

Lock disposition for the three V7-OPEN amendments:

**Amendment 1 — §3.9a thin_dimensions Free pipeline parity: LANDED.** Free unified prompt `prompt.js` ships THIN DIMENSIONS subsection inside EVIDENCE STRENGTH section + thin_dimensions schema slot in JSON STRUCTURE evidence_strength block. Tradeoffs route (`compare/tradeoffs/route.js`) and Delta route (`ideas/[id]/delta/route.js`) ship defensive sanitation helpers (`sanitizeComparisonData` + `extractEvidenceStrength` strip via destructure-rest). §3.9a Lives-In line updated to reflect both-pipelines emission; verification anchors expanded to cover Free emission rule and Tradeoffs/Delta sanitation grep gates. Same commit also caught up B6 work (`prompt-stage1.js` + `prompt-stage2a.js` profile-blind opening + SPARSE INPUT RULE + ENFORCEMENT CHECK + TEMPORAL ANCHORING) that was live in deployment but uncommitted since April 28 — git history hygiene.

**Status:** V8 OPENED at May 4, 2026 (post-V7 LOCK). **V8 LOCKED at May 4, 2026** (same day, post-V4S28 B10-prep / Haiku gate v3 collapse-pattern rescue session). One tracked surface — Amendment V8.1 — LANDED.

V8.1 closes the calibration drift surfaced during B9 thin_dimensions hygiene smoke testing. Three architectural changes shipped: (a) recalibration of pass criterion to Option A "slot presence dominates, multi-product is not a fail condition" + slot semantic rename (workflow → use_case, core_feature → mechanism, target_user retained with adoption-unit clarification) at the prompt layer; (b) system-wide rename of the slot enum across 7 files (`keywords.js`, `prompt-stage2b.js`, `prompt.js`, `analyze-pro/route.js`, `components.js`, `EvaluationView.js`, `page.js`); (c) deterministic post-FAIL collapse-pattern rescue layer in `keywords.js` for Haiku's known structural blindspot on "for X to verb-object" inputs.

**Iteration history (transparent record per V8.1 disclosure discipline):**

- **v1 (commit b52afc0)** — recalibration + system-wide rename + 14-row matrix + 86-call regression runner. Verification: 50/61 = 82% pass rate. Block A bug-trigger 5/5 ✓. Block B floor 8/8 ✓. Block D collapse 1/6 ✗ (recalibration miss — single matrix example didn't generalize). Iteration discipline triggered: pause and re-discuss design lock per B7 method.

- **v2 (commit f80b500, REVERTED)** — prompt-level fix attempt: added COLLAPSE PRINCIPLE + BUYER-CATEGORY PRINCIPLE blocks + 5 new matrix rows + "When in doubt, prefer PASS" line. Verification: catastrophic floor collapse, Block B 8/8 → 0/8. Inputs like "an app that helps people", "tool to make work easier", "I want to disrupt the legaltech industry with AI" all PASSed. Reverted via `git revert` within minutes of verification. Lesson: meta-instructions about decision posture ("prefer PASS") far more powerful than instructions about specific cases — any future calibration nudge should isolate posture-level prompt directives carefully.

- **v3 (current production)** — keep v1's prompt unchanged, add code-layer rescue in `keywords.js`. Verification: 58/61 = 95% pass rate. Block A 5/5 ✓. Block B floor 8/8 ✓ (zero regression). Block D collapse 6/6 ✓ (fully closed). All adjacent leak blocks (E, F) closed via rescue. Three documented residual false-rejects (G2, G11, K1 — all `for X that` patterns or multi-buyer cases that the conservative-scope rescue intentionally does not match). Strike count: technically failed (3 iterations across this session), but each iteration was a categorically different architectural approach (prompt rewrite → prompt edit → code-layer rescue), not the same approach repeated.

**Amendment V9.12 — Reliability invariant + Partial-State Architecture Taxonomy (NEW, V4S29).** F4's Bundle 5 cure ships 3-tier severity taxonomy (`partial_evaluation` / `degraded_evaluation` / `failed_evaluation`) with persistent flag, SSE event semantics, frontend banners, retry CTAs, Supabase schema additions.
